001package squidpony.squidmath;
002
003import squidpony.ArrayTools;
004import squidpony.StringKit;
005import squidpony.annotation.Beta;
006import squidpony.squidgrid.zone.MutableZone;
007import squidpony.squidgrid.zone.Zone;
008
009import java.io.Serializable;
010import java.util.*;
011
012/**
013 * Region encoding of on/off information about areas using bitsets; uncompressed (fatty), but fast (greased lightning).
014 * This can handle any size of 2D data, and is not strictly limited to 256x256 as CoordPacker is. It stores several long
015 * arrays and uses each bit in one of those numbers to represent a single point, though sometimes this does waste bits
016 * if the height of the area this encodes is not a multiple of 64 (if you store a 80x64 map, this uses 80 longs; if you
017 * store an 80x65 map, this uses 160 longs, 80 for the first 64 rows and 80 more to store the next row). It's much
018 * faster than CoordPacker at certain operations (anything that expands or retracts an area, including
019 * {@link #expand()}), {@link #retract()}), {@link #fringe()}), {@link #surface()}, and {@link #flood(GreasedRegion)},
020 * and slightly faster on others, like {@link #and(GreasedRegion)} (called intersectPacked() in CoordPacker) and
021 * {@link #or(GreasedRegion)} (called unionPacked() in CoordPacker).
022 * <br>
023 * Each GreasedRegion is mutable, and instance methods typically modify that instance and return it for chaining. There
024 * are exceptions, usually where multiple GreasedRegion values are returned and the instance is not modified.
025 * <br>
026 * Typical usage involves constructing a GreasedRegion from some input data, like a char[][] for a map or a double[][]
027 * from DijkstraMap, and modifying it spatially with expand(), retract(), flood(), etc. It's common to mix in data from
028 * other GreasedRegions with and() (which gets the intersection of two GreasedRegions and stores it in one), or() (which
029 * is like and() but for the union), xor() (like and() but for exclusive or, finding only cells that are on in exactly
030 * one of the two GreasedRegions), and andNot() (which can be considered the "subtract another region from me" method).
031 * There are 8-way (Chebyshev distance) variants on all of the spatial methods, and methods without "8way" in the name
032 * are either 4-way (Manhattan distance) or not affected by distance measurement. Once you have a GreasedRegion, you may
033 * want to:
034 * <ul>
035 *     <li>get a single random point from it (use {@link #singleRandom(IRNG)}),</li>
036 *     <li>get several random points from it with random sampling (use {@link #randomPortion(IRNG, int)}),</li>
037 *     <li>mutate the current GreasedRegion to keep random points from it with random sampling (use {@link #randomRegion(IRNG, int)}),</li>
038 *     <li>get random points that are likely to be separated (use {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double, int, long)} with
039 *     a random long for the last parameter, or {@link #quasiRandomSeparated(double)} if you don't want a random seed),</li>
040 *     <li>do what any of the above "separated" methods can do, but mutate the current GreasedRegion (use
041 *     {@link #mixedRandomRegion(double, int, long)} or {@link #quasiRandomRegion(double, int)}),</li>
042 *     <li>get all points from it (use {@link #asCoords()} to get a Coord array, or produce a 2D array of the contents
043 *     with {@link #decode()} or {@link #toChars(char, char)}),</li>
044 *     <li>use it to modify other 2D data, such as with {@link #mask(char[][], char)},
045 *     {@link #inverseMask(char[][], char)}, {@link #writeDoubles(double[][], double)}, or
046 *     {@link #writeIntsInto(int[][], int)}, along with variations on those.</li>
047 * </ul>
048 * <br>
049 * You may also want to produce some 2D data from one or more GreasedRegions, as with {@link #sum(GreasedRegion...)} or
050 * {@link #toChars()}. The most effective techniques regarding GreasedRegion involve multiple methods, like getting a
051 * few random points from an existing GreasedRegion representing floor tiles in a dungeon with
052 * {@link #randomRegion(IRNG, int)}, then finding a random expansion of those initial points with
053 * {@link #spill(GreasedRegion, int, IRNG)}, giving the original GreasedRegion of floor tiles as the first argument.
054 * This could be used to position puddles of water or toxic waste in a dungeon level, while still keeping the starting
055 * points and finished points within the boundaries of valid (floor) cells. If you wanted to place something like mold
056 * that can be on floors or on cells immediately adjacent to floors (like walls), you could call {@link #expand()} on
057 * the floor tiles before calling spill, allowing the spill to spread onto non-floor cells that are next to floors.
058 * <br>
059 * For efficiency, you can place one GreasedRegion into another (typically a temporary value that is no longer needed
060 * and can be recycled) using {@link #remake(GreasedRegion)}, or give the information that would normally be used to
061 * construct a fresh GreasedRegion to an existing one of the same dimensions with {@link #refill(boolean[][])} or any
062 * of the overloads of refill(). These re-methods don't do as much work as a constructor does if the width and height
063 * of their argument are identical to their current width and height, and don't create more garbage for the GC.
064 * <br>
065 * Created by Tommy Ettinger on 6/24/2016.
066 */
067@Beta
068public class GreasedRegion extends Zone.Skeleton implements Collection<Coord>, Serializable, MutableZone {
069    private static final long serialVersionUID = 0;
070    private static final SobolQRNG sobol = new SobolQRNG(2);
071
072    public long[] data;
073    public int height;
074    public int width;
075    private int ySections;
076    private long yEndMask;
077    private boolean tallied;
078    private int ct;
079    private int[] counts;
080
081    private void tally()
082    {
083        ct = 0;
084        for (int i = 0, tmp; i < counts.length; i++) {
085            tmp = Long.bitCount(data[i]);
086            counts[i] = tmp == 0 ? 0 : (ct += tmp);
087        }
088        tallied = true;
089    }
090
091    /**
092     * Constructs an empty 64x64 GreasedRegion.
093     * GreasedRegions are mutable, so you can add to this with insert() or insertSeveral(), among others.
094     */
095    public GreasedRegion()
096    {
097        width = 64;
098        height = 64;
099        ySections = 1;
100        yEndMask = -1L;
101        data = new long[64];
102        counts = new int[64];
103        ct = 0;
104        tallied = true;
105    }
106
107    /**
108     * Constructs a GreasedRegion with the given rectangular boolean array, with width of bits.length and height of
109     * bits[0].length, any value of true considered "on", and any value of false considered "off."
110     * @param bits a rectangular 2D boolean array where true is on and false is off
111     */
112    public GreasedRegion(final boolean[][] bits)
113    {
114        width = bits.length;
115        height = bits[0].length;
116        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
117        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
118        data = new long[width * ySections];
119        for (int x = 0, xs = 0; x < width; x++, xs += ySections) {
120            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
121                if(bits[x][y]) data[xs + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
122            }
123        }
124        counts = new int[width * ySections];
125        tallied = false;
126    }
127    /**
128     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion with the given rectangular boolean array, reusing the current data storage (without
129     * extra allocations) if this.width == map.length and this.height == map[0].length. The current values stored in
130     * this are always cleared, then any value of true in map is considered "on", and any value of false in map is
131     * considered "off."
132     * @param map a rectangular 2D boolean array where true is on and false is off
133     * @return this for chaining
134     */
135    public GreasedRegion refill(final boolean[][] map) {
136        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && width == map.length && height == map[0].length) {
137            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
138            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
139                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
140                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= (map[x][y] ? 1L : 0L) << (y & 63);
141                }
142            }
143            tallied = false;
144            return this;
145        } else {
146            width = (map == null) ? 0 : map.length;
147            height = (map == null || map.length <= 0) ? 0 : map[0].length;
148            ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
149            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
150            data = new long[width * ySections];
151            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
152                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
153                    if(map[x][y]) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
154                }
155            }
156            counts = new int[width * ySections];
157            tallied = false;
158            return this;
159        }
160    }
161
162    /**
163     * Constructs a GreasedRegion with the given rectangular char array, with width of map.length and height of
164     * map[0].length, any value that equals yes is considered "on", and any other value considered "off."
165     * @param map a rectangular 2D char array where yes is on and everything else is off
166     * @param yes which char to encode as "on"
167     */
168    public GreasedRegion(final char[][] map, final char yes)
169    {
170        width = map.length;
171        height = map[0].length;
172        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
173        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
174        data = new long[width * ySections];
175        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
176            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
177                if(map[x][y] == yes) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
178            }
179        }
180        counts = new int[width * ySections];
181        tallied = false;
182    }
183    /**
184     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion with the given rectangular char array, reusing the current data storage (without
185     * extra allocations) if this.width == map.length and this.height == map[0].length. The current values stored in
186     * this are always cleared, then any value that equals yes is considered "on", and any other value considered "off."
187     * @param map a rectangular 2D char array where yes is on and everything else is off
188     * @param yes which char to encode as "on"
189     * @return this for chaining
190     */
191    public GreasedRegion refill(final char[][] map, final char yes) {
192        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && width == map.length && height == map[0].length) {
193            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
194            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
195                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
196                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= ((map[x][y] == yes) ? 1L : 0L) << (y & 63);
197                }
198            }
199            tallied = false;
200            return this;
201        } else {
202            width = (map == null) ? 0 : map.length;
203            height = (map == null || map.length <= 0) ? 0 : map[0].length;
204            ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
205            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
206            data = new long[width * ySections];
207            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
208                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
209                    if(map[x][y] == yes) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
210                }
211            }
212            counts = new int[width * ySections];
213            tallied = false;
214            return this;
215        }
216    }

218    /**
219     * Weird constructor that takes a String array, _as it would be printed_, so each String is a row and indexing would
220     * be done with y, x instead of the normal x, y.
221     * @param map String array (as printed, not the normal storage) where each String is a row
222     * @param yes the char to consider "on" in the GreasedRegion
223     */
224    public GreasedRegion(final String[] map, final char yes)
225    {
226        height = map.length;
227        width = map[0].length();
228        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
229        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
230        data = new long[width * ySections];
231        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
232            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
233                if(map[y].charAt(x) == yes) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
234            }
235        }
236        counts = new int[width * ySections];
237        tallied = false;
238    }
239
240    /**
241     * Weird refill method that takes a String array, _as it would be printed_, so each String is a row and indexing
242     * would be done with y, x instead of the normal x, y.
243     * @param map String array (as printed, not the normal storage) where each String is a row
244     * @param yes the char to consider "on" in the GreasedRegion
245     * @return this for chaining
246     */
247    public GreasedRegion refill(final String[] map, final char yes) {
248        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && height == map.length && width == map[0].length()) {
249            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
250            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
251                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
252                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= ((map[y].charAt(x) == yes) ? 1L : 0L) << (y & 63);
253                }
254            }
255            tallied = false;
256            return this;
257        } else {
258            height = (map == null) ? 0 : map.length;
259            width = (map == null || map.length <= 0) ? 0 : map[0].length();
260            ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
261            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
262            data = new long[width * ySections];
263            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
264                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
265                    if(map[y].charAt(y) == yes) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
266                }
267            }
268            counts = new int[width * ySections];
269            tallied = false;
270            return this;
271        }
272    }
273    /**
274     * Constructs a GreasedRegion with the given rectangular int array, with width of map.length and height of
275     * map[0].length, any value that equals yes is considered "on", and any other value considered "off."
276     * @param map a rectangular 2D int array where an int == yes is on and everything else is off
277     * @param yes which int to encode as "on"
278     */
279    public GreasedRegion(final int[][] map, final int yes)
280    {
281        width = map.length;
282        height = map[0].length;
283        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
284        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
285        data = new long[width * ySections];
286        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
287            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
288                if(map[x][y] == yes) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
289            }
290        }
291        counts = new int[width * ySections];
292        tallied = false;
293    }

295     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion with the given rectangular int array, reusing the current data storage (without

299     * @param yes which int to encode as "on"
300     * @return this for chaining
301     */
302    public GreasedRegion refill(final int[][] map, final int yes) {
303        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && width == map.length && height == map[0].length) {
304            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
305            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {

308                }

328
329    /**
330     * Constructs this GreasedRegion using an int[][], treating cells as on if they are greater than or equal to lower
331     * and less than upper, or off otherwise.
332     * @param map an int[][] that should have some ints between lower and upper
333     * @param lower lower bound, inclusive; all on cells will have values in map that are at least equal to lower
334     * @param upper upper bound, exclusive; all on cells will have values in map that are less than upper
335     */
336    public GreasedRegion(final int[][] map, final int lower, final int upper)
337    {
338        width = map.length;
339        height = map[0].length;
340        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
341        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
342        data = new long[width * ySections];
343        int[] column;
344        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
345            column = map[x];
346            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
347                if(column[y] >= lower && column[y] < upper) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
348            }
349        }
350        counts = new int[width * ySections];
351        tallied = false;
352    }
353
354    /**
355     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion with the given rectangular int array, reusing the current data storage (without
356     * extra allocations) if this.width == map.length and this.height == map[0].length. The current values stored in
357     * this are always cleared, then cells are treated as on if they are greater than or equal to lower and less than
358     * upper, or off otherwise.
359     * @param map a rectangular 2D int array that should have some values between lower and upper
360     * @param lower lower bound, inclusive; all on cells will have values in map that are at least equal to lower
361     * @param upper upper bound, exclusive; all on cells will have values in map that are less than upper
362     * @return this for chaining
363     */
364    public GreasedRegion refill(final int[][] map, final int lower, final int upper) {
365        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && width == map.length && height == map[0].length) {
366            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
367            int[] column;
368            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
369                column = map[x];
370                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
371                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= ((column[y] >= lower && column[y] < upper) ? 1L : 0L) << (y & 63);
372                }
373            }
374            tallied = false;
375            return this;
376        } else {
377            width = (map == null) ? 0 : map.length;
378            height = (map == null || map.length <= 0) ? 0 : map[0].length;
379            ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
380            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
381            data = new long[width * ySections];
382            int[] column;
383            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
384                column = map[x];
385                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
386                    if(column[y] >= lower && column[y] < upper) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
387                }
388            }
389            counts = new int[width * ySections];
390            tallied = false;
391            return this;
392        }
393    }

401     */
