1813
1814    public GreasedRegion removeRectangle(int startX, int startY, int rectangleWidth, int rectangleHeight)
1815    {
1816        if(startX < 0)
1817        {
1818            rectangleWidth += startX;
1819            startX = 0;
1820        }
1821        else if(startX >= width)
1822        {
1823            rectangleWidth = 1;
1824            startX = width - 1;
1825        }
1826        if(startY < 0)
1827        {
1828            rectangleHeight += startY;
1829            startY = 0;
1830        }
1831        else if(startY >= height)
1832        {
1833            rectangleHeight = 1;
1834            startY = height - 1;
1835        }
1836        if(rectangleWidth < 1 || rectangleHeight < 1 || ySections <= 0)
1837            return this;
1838        int endX = Math.min(width, startX + rectangleWidth) - 1,
1839                endY = Math.min(height, startY + rectangleHeight) - 1,
1840                startSection = startY >> 6, endSection = endY >> 6;
1841        if(startSection < endSection)
1842        {
1843            long startMask = ~(-1L << (startY & 63)),
1844                    endMask = ~(-1L >>> (~endY & 63));
1845            for (int a = startX * ySections + startSection; a <= endX * ySections + startSection; a += ySections) {
1846                data[a] &= startMask;
1847            }
1848            if(endSection - startSection > 1)
1849            {
1850                for (int b = 1; b < endSection - startSection; b++) {
1851                    for (int a = startX * ySections + startSection + b; a < endX * ySections + ySections; a += ySections) {
1852                        data[a] = 0;
1853                    }
1854                }
1855            }
1856            for (int a = startX * ySections + endSection; a <= endX * ySections + endSection; a += ySections) {
1857                data[a] &= endMask;
1858            }
1859        }
1860        else
1861        {
1862            long mask = ~((-1L << (startY & 63)) & (-1L >>> (~endY & 63)));
1863            for (int a = startX * ySections + startSection; a <= endX * ySections + startSection; a += ySections) {
1864                data[a] &= mask;
1865            }
1866        }
1867        tallied = false;
1868        return this;
1869    }
1870
1871    public GreasedRegion removeCircle(Coord center, int radius)
1872    {
1873        float high, changedX;
1874        int rndX, rndY;
1875        for (int dx = -radius; dx <= radius; ++dx) {
1876            changedX = dx - 0.25f * Math.signum(dx);
1877            rndX = Math.round(changedX);
1878            high = (float) Math.sqrt(radius * radius - changedX * changedX);
1879            remove(center.x + rndX, center.y);
1880            for (float dy = high; dy >= 0.75f; --dy) {
1881                rndY = Math.round(dy - 0.25f);
1882                remove(center.x + rndX, center.y + rndY);
1883                remove(center.x + rndX, center.y - rndY);
1884            }
1885        }
1886        return this;
1887    }
1888
1889    /**
1890     * Equivalent to {@link #clear()}, setting all cells to "off," but also returns this for chaining.
1891     * @return this for chaining
1892     */
1893    public GreasedRegion empty()
1894    {
1895        Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
1896        Arrays.fill(counts, 0);
1897        ct = 0;
1898        tallied = true;
1899        return this;
1900    }
1901
1902    /**
1903     * Sets all cells in this to "on."
1904     * @return this for chaining
1905     */
1906    public GreasedRegion allOn()
1907    {
1908        if(ySections > 0)
1909        {
1910            if(yEndMask == -1) {
1911                Arrays.fill(data, -1);
1912                Arrays.fill(counts, 64);
1913                ct = ySections * width << 6;
1914                tallied = true;
1915            }
1916            else
1917            {
1918                ct = Long.bitCount(yEndMask);
1919                for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
1920                    data[a] = yEndMask;
1921                    counts[a] = ct;
1922                    for (int i = 0; i < ySections - 1; i++) {
1923                        data[a-i-1] = -1;
1924                        counts[a-i-1] = 64;
1925                    }
1926                }
1927                ct *= width;
1928                ct += (ySections - 1) * width << 6;
1929                tallied = true;
1930            }
1931        }
1932        return this;
1933    }
1934
1935    /**
1936     * Sets all cells in this to "on" if contents is true, or "off" if contents is false.
1937     * @param contents true to set all cells to on, false to set all cells to off
1938     * @return this for chaining
1939     */
1940    public GreasedRegion fill(boolean contents)
1941    {
1942        if(contents)
1943        {
1944            if(ySections > 0)
1945            {
1946                if(yEndMask == -1) {
1947                    Arrays.fill(data, -1);
1948                    Arrays.fill(counts, 64);
1949                    ct = ySections * width << 6;
1950                    tallied = true;
1951                }
1952                else
1953                {
1954                    ct = Long.bitCount(yEndMask);
1955                    for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
1956                        data[a] = yEndMask;
1957                        counts[a] = ct;
1958                        for (int i = 0; i < ySections - 1; i++) {
1959                            data[a-i-1] = -1;
1960                            counts[a-i-1] = 64;
1961                        }
1962                    }
1963                    ct *= width;
1964                    ct += (ySections - 1) * width << 6;
1965                    tallied = true;
1966                }
1967            }
1968            //else... what, if ySections is 0 there's nothing to do
1969        }
1970        else
1971        {
1972            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
1973            Arrays.fill(counts, 0);
1974            ct = 0;
1975            tallied = true;
1976        }
1977        return this;
1978    }
1979    /**
1980     * Turns all cells that are adjacent to the boundaries of the GreasedRegion to "off".
1981     * @return this for chaining
1982     */
1983    public GreasedRegion removeEdges()
1984    {
1985        if(ySections > 0) {
1986            for (int i = 0; i < ySections; i++) {
1987                data[i] = 0L;
1988                data[width * ySections - 1 - i] = 0L;
1989            }
1990            if (ySections == 1) {
1991                for (int i = 0; i < width; i++) {
1992                    data[i] &= yEndMask >>> 1 & -2L;
1993                }
1994            } else {
1995                for (int i = ySections; i < data.length - ySections; i += ySections) {
1996                    data[i] &= -2L;
1997                }
1998                for (int a = ySections * 2 - 1; a < data.length - ySections; a += ySections) {
1999                    data[a] &= yEndMask >>> 1;
2000                }
2001            }
2002            tallied = false;
2003        }
2004        return this;
2005    }
2006
2007    /**
2008     * Simple method that returns a newly-allocated copy of this GreasedRegion; modifications to one won't change the
2009     * other, and this method returns the copy while leaving the original unchanged.
2010     * @return a copy of this GreasedRegion; the copy can be changed without altering the original
2011     */
2012    public GreasedRegion copy()
2013    {
2014        return new GreasedRegion(this);
2015    }
2016
2017    /**
2018     * Returns this GreasedRegion's data as a 2D boolean array, [width][height] in size, with on treated as true and off
2019     * treated as false.
2020     * @return a 2D boolean array that represents this GreasedRegion's data
2021     */
2022    public boolean[][] decode()
2023    {
2024        boolean[][] bools = new boolean[width][height];
2025        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
2026            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
2027                bools[x][y] = (data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0;
2028            }
2029        }
2030        return bools;
2031    }
2032
2033    /**
2034     * Fills this GreasedRegion's data into the given 2D char array, modifying it and returning it, with "on" cells
2035     * filled with the char parameter {@code on} and "off" cells with the parameter {@code off}.
2036     * @param chars a 2D char array that will be modified; must not be null, nor can it contain null elements
2037     * @param on the char to use for "on" cells
2038     * @param off the char to use for "off" cells
2039     * @return a 2D char array that represents this GreasedRegion's data
2040     */
2041    public char[][] intoChars(char[][] chars, char on, char off)
2042    {
2043        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < chars.length; x++) {
2044            for (int y = 0; y < height && y < chars[x].length; y++) {
2045                chars[x][y] = (data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? on : off;
2046            }
2047        }
2048        return chars;
2049    }
2050
2051    /**
2052     * Fills this GreasedRegion's data into the given 2D char array, modifying it and returning it, with "on" cells
2053     * filled with the char parameter {@code on} and "off" cells left as-is.
2054     * @param chars a 2D char array that will be modified; must not be null, nor can it contain null elements
2055     * @param on the char to use for "on" cells
2056     * @return a 2D char array that represents the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion's data written over chars
2057     */
2058    public char[][] intoChars(char[][] chars, char on)
2059    {
2060        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < chars.length; x++) {
2061            for (int y = 0; y < height && y < chars[x].length; y++) {
2062                if((data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0)
2063                    chars[x][y] = on;
2064            }
2065        }
2066        return chars;
2067    }
2068
2069    /**
2070     * Returns this GreasedRegion's data as a 2D char array,  [width][height] in size, with "on" cells filled with the
2071     * char parameter on and "off" cells with the parameter off.
2072     * @param on the char to use for "on" cells
2073     * @param off the char to use for "off" cells
2074     * @return a 2D char array that represents this GreasedRegion's data
2075     */
2076    public char[][] toChars(char on, char off)
2077    {
2078        char[][] chars = new char[width][height];
2079        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
2080            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
2081                chars[x][y] = (data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? on : off;
2082            }
2083        }
2084        return chars;
2085    }
2086    /**
2087     * Returns this GreasedRegion's data as a 2D char array,  [width][height] in size, with "on" cells filled with '.'
2088     * and "off" cells with '#'.
2089     * @return a 2D char array that represents this GreasedRegion's data
2090     */
2091
2092    public char[][] toChars()
2093    {
2094        return toChars('.', '#');
2095    }

2097    /**
2098     * Returns this GreasedRegion's data as a StringBuilder, with each row made of the parameter on for "on" cells and
2099     * the parameter off for "off" cells, separated by newlines, with no trailing newline at the end.
2100     * @param on the char to use for "on" cells
2101     * @param off the char to use for "off" cells
2102     * @return a StringBuilder that stores each row of this GreasedRegion as chars, with rows separated by newlines.
2103     */
2104    public StringBuilder show(char on, char off)
2105    {
2106        StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder((width+1) * height);
2107        for (int y = 0; y < height;) {
2108            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
2109                sb.append((data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? on : off);
2110            }
2111            if(++y < height)
2112                sb.append('\n');
2113        }
2114        return sb;
2115    }

2117    /**
2118     * Returns a legible String representation of this that can be printed over multiple lines, with all "on" cells
2119     * represented by '.' and all "off" cells by '#', in roguelike floors-on walls-off convention, separating each row
2120     * by newlines (without a final trailing newline, so you could append text right after this).
2121     * @return a String representation of this GreasedRegion using '.' for on, '#' for off, and newlines between rows
2122     */
2123    @Override
2124    public String toString()
2125    {
2126        return show('.', '#').toString();
2127    }

2129    /**
2130     * Returns a copy of map where if a cell is "on" in this GreasedRegion, this keeps the value in map intact,
2131     * and where a cell is "off", it instead writes the char filler.
2132     * @param map a 2D char array that will not be modified
2133     * @param filler the char to use where this GreasedRegion stores an "off" cell
2134     * @return a masked copy of map
2135     */
2136    public char[][] mask(char[][] map, char filler)
2137    {
2138        if(map == null || map.length == 0)
2139            return new char[0][0];
2140        int width2 = Math.min(width, map.length), height2 = Math.min(height, map[0].length);
2141        char[][] chars = new char[width2][height2];
2142        for (int x = 0; x < width2; x++) {
2143            for (int y = 0; y < height2; y++) {
2144                chars[x][y] = (data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? map[x][y] : filler;
2145            }
2146        }
2147        return chars;
2148    }

2157     */
2158    public short[][] mask(short[][] map, short filler)

2161            return new short[0][0];

2163        short[][] shorts = new short[width2][height2];
2164        for (int x = 0; x < width2; x++) {
2165            for (int y = 0; y < height2; y++) {
2166                shorts[x][y] = (data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? map[x][y] : filler;
2167            }
2168        }
2169        return shorts;
2170    }

2173     * Returns a copy of map where if a cell is "off" in this GreasedRegion, this keeps the value in map intact,

2176     * @param toWrite the char to use where this GreasedRegion stores an "on" cell
2177     * @return a masked copy of map
2178     */
2179    public char[][] inverseMask(char[][] map, char toWrite)
2180    {
2181        if(map == null || map.length == 0)
2182            return new char[0][0];
2183        int width2 = Math.min(width, map.length), height2 = Math.min(height, map[0].length);
2184        char[][] chars = new char[width2][height2];
2185        for (int x = 0; x < width2; x++) {
2186            for (int y = 0; y < height2; y++) {
2187                chars[x][y] = (data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? toWrite : map[x][y];
2188            }
2189        }

2209            }

2214    /**
2215     * "Inverse mask for ints;" returns a copy of map where if a cell is "off" in this GreasedRegion, this keeps
2216     * the value in map intact, and where a cell is "on", it instead writes the int toWrite. Modifies map in-place,
2217     * unlike {@link #writeInts(int[][], int)}.
2218     * @param map a 2D int array that <b>will</b> be modified
2219     * @param toWrite the int to use where this GreasedRegion stores an "on" cell
2220     * @return map, with the changes applied; not a copy
2221     */
2222    public int[][] writeIntsInto(int[][] map, int toWrite)
2223    {
2224        if(map == null || map.length == 0)
2225            return map;
2226        int width2 = Math.min(width, map.length), height2 = Math.min(height, map[0].length);
2227        for (int x = 0; x < width2; x++) {
2228            for (int y = 0; y < height2; y++) {
2229                if((data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0)
2230                    map[x][y] = toWrite;
2231            }
2232        }
2233        return map;
2234    }

2299    /**
2300     * Union of two GreasedRegions, assigning the result into this GreasedRegion. Any cell that is "on" in either
2301     * GreasedRegion will be made "on" in this GreasedRegion.
2302     * @param other another GreasedRegion that will not be modified
2303     * @return this, after modification, for chaining
2304     */
2305    public GreasedRegion or(GreasedRegion other)
2306    {
2307        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < other.width; x++) {
2308            for (int y = 0; y < ySections && y < other.ySections; y++) {
2309                data[x * ySections + y] |= other.data[x * ySections + y];
2310            }
2311        }
2312
2313        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
2314            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
2315                data[a] &= yEndMask;
2316            }
2317        }
2318        tallied = false;
2319
2320        return this;
2321    }
2322
2323    /**
2324     * Intersection of two GreasedRegions, assigning the result into this GreasedRegion. Any cell that is "on" in both
2325     * GreasedRegions will be kept "on" in this GreasedRegion, but all other cells will be made "off."
2326     * @param other another GreasedRegion that will not be modified
2327     * @return this, after modification, for chaining
2328     */
2329    public GreasedRegion and(GreasedRegion other)
2330    {
2331        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < other.width; x++) {
2332            for (int y = 0; y < ySections && y < other.ySections; y++) {
2333                data[x * ySections + y] &= other.data[x * ySections + y];
2334            }
2335        }
2336        tallied = false;
2337        return this;
2338    }
2339    /**
2340     * Difference of two GreasedRegions, assigning the result into this GreasedRegion. Any cell that is "on" in this
2341     * GreasedRegion and "off" in other will be kept "on" in this GreasedRegion, but all other cells will be made "off."
2342     * @param other another GreasedRegion that will not be modified
2343     * @return this, after modification, for chaining
2344     * @see #notAnd(GreasedRegion) notAnd is a very similar method that acts sort-of in reverse of this method
2345     */
2346    public GreasedRegion andNot(GreasedRegion other)
2347    {
2348        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < other.width; x++) {
2349            for (int y = 0; y < ySections && y < other.ySections; y++) {
2350                data[x * ySections + y] &= ~other.data[x * ySections + y];
2351            }
2352        }
2353        tallied = false;
2354        return this;
2355    }
2356
2357    /**
2358     * Like andNot, but subtracts this GreasedRegion from other and stores the result in this GreasedRegion, without
2359     * mutating other.
2360     * @param other another GreasedRegion that will not be modified
2361     * @return this, after modification, for chaining
2362     * @see #andNot(GreasedRegion) andNot is a very similar method that acts sort-of in reverse of this method
2363     */
2364    public GreasedRegion notAnd(GreasedRegion other)
2365    {
2366        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < other.width; x++) {
2367            for (int y = 0; y < ySections && y < other.ySections; y++) {
2368                data[x * ySections + y] = other.data[x * ySections + y] & ~data[x * ySections + y];
2369            }
2370        }
2371        tallied = false;
2372        return this;
2373    }

2375    /**
2376     * Symmetric difference (more commonly known as exclusive or, hence the name) of two GreasedRegions, assigning the
2377     * result into this GreasedRegion. Any cell that is "on" in this and "off" in other, or "off" in this and "on" in
2378     * other, will be made "on" in this; all other cells will be made "off." Useful to find cells that are "on" in
2379     * exactly one of two GreasedRegions (not "on" in both, or "off" in both).
2380     * @param other another GreasedRegion that will not be modified
2381     * @return this, after modification, for chaining
2382     */
2383    public GreasedRegion xor(GreasedRegion other)
2384    {
2385        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < other.width; x++) {
2386            for (int y = 0; y < ySections && y < other.ySections; y++) {
2387                data[x * ySections + y] ^= other.data[x * ySections + y];
2388            }
2389        }
2390
2391        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
2392            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
2393                data[a] &= yEndMask;
2394            }
2395        }
2396        tallied = false;
2397        return this;
2398    }
2399
2400    /**
2401     * Negates this GreasedRegion, turning "on" to "off" and "off" to "on."
2402     * @return this, after modification, for chaining
2403     */
2404    public GreasedRegion not()
2405    {
2406        for (int a = 0; a < data.length; a++)
2407        {
2408            data[a] = ~data[a];
2409        }
2410
2411        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
2412            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
2413                data[a] &= yEndMask;
2414            }
2415        }
2416        tallied = false;
2417        return this;
2418    }
2419
2420    /**
2421     * Moves the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion to the given x and y offset, removing cells that move out of bounds.
2422     * @param x the x offset to translate by; can be negative
2423     * @param y the y offset to translate by; can be negative
2424     * @return this for chaining
2425     */
2426    public GreasedRegion translate(int x, int y)
2427    {
2428        if(width < 1 || ySections <= 0 || (x == 0 && y == 0))
2429            return this;
2430        int start = Math.max(0, x), len = Math.min(width, width + x) - start,
2431                jump = (y == 0) ? 0 : (y < 0) ? -(1-y >>> 6) : (y-1 >>> 6), lily = (y < 0) ? -(-y & 63) : (y & 63),
2432                originalJump = Math.max(0, -jump), alterJump = Math.max(0, jump);
2433        long[] data2 = new long[width * ySections];
2434
2435        long prev, tmp;
2436        if (x < 0) {
2437            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2438                for (int j = Math.max(0, -x), jj = 0; jj < len; j++, jj++) {
2439                    data2[jj * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2440                }
2441            }
2442        } else if (x > 0) {
2443            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2444                for (int j = 0, jj = start; j < len; j++, jj++) {
2445                    data2[jj * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2446                }
2447            }
2448        } else {
2449            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2450                for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
2451                    data2[j * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2452                }
2453            }
2454        }
2455
2456        if(lily < 0) {
2457            for (int i = start; i < len; i++) {
2458                prev = 0L;
2459                for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
2460                    tmp = prev;
2461                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L << -lily)) << (64 + lily);
2462                    data2[i * ySections + j] >>>= -lily;
2463                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
2464                }
2465            }
2466        }
2467        else if(lily > 0) {
2468            for (int i = start; i < start + len; i++) {
2469                prev = 0L;
2470                for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
2471                    tmp = prev;
2472                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L >>> lily)) >>> (64 - lily);
2473                    data2[i * ySections + j] <<= lily;
2474                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
2475                }
2476            }
2477        }
2478
2479
2480        if(yEndMask != -1) {
2481            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data2.length; a += ySections) {
2482                data2[a] &= yEndMask;
2483            }
2484        }
2485
2486        data = data2;
2487        tallied = false;
2488        return this;
2489    }
2490
2491    /**
2492     * Adds to this GreasedRegion with a moved set of its own "on" cells, moved to the given x and y offset.
2493     * Ignores cells that would be added out of bounds. Keeps all cells that are currently "on" unchanged.
2494     * @param x the x offset to translate by; can be negative
2495     * @param y the y offset to translate by; can be negative
2496     * @return this for chaining
2497     */
2498    public GreasedRegion insertTranslation(int x, int y)
2499    {
2500        if(width < 1 || ySections <= 0 || (x == 0 && y == 0))
2501            return this;
2502        int start = Math.max(0, x), len = Math.min(width, width + x) - start,
2503                jump = (y == 0) ? 0 : (y < 0) ? -(1-y >>> 6) : (y-1 >>> 6), lily = (y < 0) ? -(-y & 63) : (y & 63),
2504                originalJump = Math.max(0, -jump), alterJump = Math.max(0, jump);
2505        long[] data2 = new long[width * ySections];
2506        long prev, tmp;
2507        if (x < 0) {
2508            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2509                for (int j = Math.max(0, -x), jj = 0; jj < len; j++, jj++) {
2510                    data2[jj * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2511                }
2512            }
2513        } else if (x > 0) {
2514            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2515                for (int j = 0, jj = start; j < len; j++, jj++) {
2516                    data2[jj * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2517                }
2518            }
2519        } else {
2520            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2521                for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
2522                    data2[j * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2523                }
2524            }
2525        }
2526
2527        if(lily < 0) {
2528            for (int i = start; i < len; i++) {
2529                prev = 0L;
2530                for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
2531                    tmp = prev;
2532                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L << -lily)) << (64 + lily);
2533                    data2[i * ySections + j] >>>= -lily;
2534                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
2535                }
2536            }
2537        }
2538        else if(lily > 0) {
2539            for (int i = start; i < start + len; i++) {
2540                prev = 0L;
2541                for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
2542                    tmp = prev;
2543                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L >>> lily)) >>> (64 - lily);
2544                    data2[i * ySections + j] <<= lily;
2545                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
2546                }
2547            }
2548        }
2549
2550        for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
2551            data2[i] |= data[i];
2552        }
2553
2554
2555        if(yEndMask != -1) {
2556            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data2.length; a += ySections) {
2557                data2[a] &= yEndMask;
2558            }
2559        }
2560
2561        data = data2;
2562        tallied = false;
2563        return this;
2564    }
2565
2566    /**
2567     * Effectively doubles the x and y values of each cell this contains (not scaling each cell to be larger, so each
2568     * "on" cell will be surrounded by "off" cells), and re-maps the positions so the given x and y in the doubled space
2569     * become 0,0 in the resulting GreasedRegion (which is this, assigning to itself).
2570     * @param x in the doubled coordinate space, the x position that should become 0 x in the result; can be negative
2571     * @param y in the doubled coordinate space, the y position that should become 0 y in the result; can be negative
2572     * @return this for chaining
2573     */
2574    public GreasedRegion zoom(int x, int y)
2575    {
2576        if(width < 1 || ySections <= 0)
2577            return this;
2578        x = -x;
2579        y = -y;
2580        int
2581                width2 = width + 1 >>> 1, ySections2 = ySections + 1 >>> 1,
2582                start = Math.max(0, x), len = Math.min(width, width + x) - start,
2583                //tall = (Math.min(height, height + y) - Math.max(0, y)) + 63 >> 6,
2584                jump = (y == 0) ? 0 : (y < 0) ? -(1-y >>> 6) : (y-1 >>> 6), lily = (y < 0) ? -(-y & 63) : (y & 63),
2585                originalJump = Math.max(0, -jump), alterJump = Math.max(0, jump),
2586                oddX = (x & 1), oddY = (y & 1);
2587        long[] data2 = new long[width * ySections];
2588
2589        long prev, tmp, yEndMask2 = -1L >>> (64 - ((height + 1 >>> 1) & 63));
2590        if (x < 0) {
2591            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i <= ySections2 && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2592                for (int j = Math.max(0, -x), jj = 0; jj < len; j++, jj++) {
2593                    data2[jj * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2594                }
2595            }
2596        } else if (x > 0) {
2597            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i <= ySections2 && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2598                for (int j = 0, jj = start; j < len; j++, jj++) {
2599                    data2[jj * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2600                }
2601            }
2602        } else {
2603            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i <= ySections2 && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2604                for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
2605                    data2[j * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2606                }
2607            }
2608        }
2609
2610        if(lily < 0) {
2611            for (int i = start; i < len; i++) {
2612                prev = 0L;
2613                for (int j = ySections2; j >= 0; j--) {
2614                    tmp = prev;
2615                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L << -lily)) << (64 + lily);
2616                    data2[i * ySections + j] >>>= -lily;
2617                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
2618                }
2619            }
2620        }
2621        else if(lily > 0) {
2622            for (int i = start; i < start + len; i++) {
2623                prev = 0L;
2624                for (int j = 0; j < ySections2; j++) {
2625                    tmp = prev;
2626                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L >>> lily)) >>> (64 - lily);
2627                    data2[i * ySections + j] <<= lily;
2628                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
2629                }
2630            }
2631        }
2632
2633
2634        if(ySections2 > 0 && yEndMask2 != -1) {
2635            for (int a = ySections2 - 1; a < data2.length; a += ySections) {
2636                data2[a] &= yEndMask2;
2637                if(ySections2 < ySections)
2638                    data2[a+1] = 0L;
2639            }
2640        }
2641        for (int i = 0; i < width2; i++) {
2642            for (int j = 0; j < ySections2; j++) {
2643                prev = data2[i * ySections + j];
2644                tmp = prev >>> 32;
2645                prev &= 0xFFFFFFFFL;
2646                prev = (prev | (prev << 16)) & 0x0000FFFF0000FFFFL;
2647                prev = (prev | (prev << 8)) & 0x00FF00FF00FF00FFL;
2648                prev = (prev | (prev << 4)) & 0x0F0F0F0F0F0F0F0FL;
2649                prev = (prev | (prev << 2)) & 0x3333333333333333L;
2650                prev = (prev | (prev << 1)) & 0x5555555555555555L;
2651                prev <<= oddY;
2652                if(oddX == 1) {
2653                    if (i * 2 + 1 < width)
2654                        data[(i * ySections + j) * 2 + ySections] = prev;
2655                    if (i * 2 < width)
2656                        data[(i * ySections + j) * 2] = 0L;
2657                }
2658                else
2659                {
2660                    if (i * 2 < width)
2661                        data[(i * ySections + j) * 2] = prev;
2662                    if (i * 2 + 1 < width)
2663                        data[(i * ySections + j) * 2 + ySections] = 0L;
2664                }
2665                if(j * 2 + 1 < ySections) {
2666                    tmp = (tmp | (tmp << 16)) & 0x0000FFFF0000FFFFL;
2667                    tmp = (tmp | (tmp << 8)) & 0x00FF00FF00FF00FFL;
2668                    tmp = (tmp | (tmp << 4)) & 0x0F0F0F0F0F0F0F0FL;
2669                    tmp = (tmp | (tmp << 2)) & 0x3333333333333333L;
2670                    tmp = (tmp | (tmp << 1)) & 0x5555555555555555L;
2671                    tmp <<= oddY;
2672                    if(oddX == 1) {
2673                        if (i * 2 + 1 < width)
2674                            data[(i * ySections + j) * 2 + ySections + 1] = tmp;
2675                        if (i * 2 < width)
2676                            data[(i * ySections + j) * 2 + 1] = 0L;
2677                    }
2678                    else
2679                    {
2680                        if (i * 2 < width)
2681                            data[(i * ySections + j) * 2 + 1] = tmp;
2682                        if (i * 2 + 1 < width)
2683                            data[(i * ySections + j) * 2 + ySections + 1] = 0L;
2684                    }
2685                }
2686            }
2687        }
2688
2689        if(yEndMask != -1) {
2690            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
2691                data[a] &= yEndMask;
2692            }
2693        }
2694        tallied = false;
2695        return this;
2696    }
2697
2698    /**
2699     * Takes the pairs of "on" cells in this GreasedRegion that are separated by exactly one cell in an orthogonal line,
2700     * and changes the gap cells to "on" as well.
2701     * <br>
2702     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
2703     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
2704     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
2705     * @return this for chaining
2706     */
2707    public GreasedRegion connect()
2708    {
2709        if(width < 2 || ySections == 0)
2710            return this;
2711
2712        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
2713        System.arraycopy(data, 0, next, 0, width * ySections);
2714        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
2715            next[a] |= ((data[a] << 1) & (data[a] >>> 1)) | data[a+ySections];
2716            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= ((data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1) & (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1)) | data[(width-2) *ySections+a];
2717
2718            for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2719                next[i] |= ((data[i] << 1) & (data[i] >>> 1)) | (data[i - ySections] & data[i + ySections]);
2720            }
2721
2722            if(a > 0) {
2723                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2724                    next[i] |= (data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i] >>> 1);
2725                }
2726            }
2727            else
2728            {
2729                for (int i = ySections; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2730                    next[i] |= (data[i] >>> 1 & 1L);
2731                }
2732            }
2733
2734            if(a < ySections - 1) {
2735                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2736                    next[i] |= (data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i] << 1);
2737                }
2738            }
2739            else
2740            {
2741                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2742                    next[i] |= (data[i] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L);
2743                }
2744
2745            }
2746        }
2747
2748        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
2749            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
2750                next[a] &= yEndMask;
2751            }
2752        }
2753        data = next;
2754        tallied = false;
2755        return this;
2756    }
2757
2758    /**
2759     * Takes the pairs of "on" cells in this GreasedRegion that are separated by exactly one cell in an orthogonal or
2760     * diagonal line, and changes the gap cells to "on" as well.
2761     * <br>
2762     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
2763     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
2764     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
2765     * @return this for chaining
2766     */
2767    public GreasedRegion connect8way()
2768    {
2769        if(width < 2 || ySections == 0)
2770            return this;
2771
2772        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
2773        System.arraycopy(data, 0, next, 0, width * ySections);
2774        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
2775            next[a] |= ((data[a] << 1) & (data[a] >>> 1)) | data[a+ySections] | (data[a+ySections] << 1) | (data[a+ySections] >>> 1);
2776            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= ((data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1) & (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1))
2777                    | data[(width-2) *ySections+a] | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] >>> 1);
2778
2779            for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2780                next[i] |= ((data[i] << 1) & (data[i] >>> 1)) | (data[i - ySections] & data[i + ySections])
2781                        | ((data[i - ySections] << 1) & (data[i + ySections] >>> 1))
2782                        | ((data[i + ySections] << 1) & (data[i - ySections] >>> 1));
2783            }
2784
2785            if(a > 0) {
2786                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2787                    next[i] |= ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i] >>> 1)) |
2788                            ((data[i - ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i + ySections] >>> 1)) |
2789                            ((data[i + ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i - ySections] >>> 1));
2790                }
2791            }
2792            else
2793            {
2794                for (int i = ySections; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2795                    next[i] |= (data[i] >>> 1 & 1L) | (data[i - ySections] >>> 1 & 1L) | (data[i + ySections] >>> 1 & 1L);
2796                }
2797            }
2798
2799            if(a < ySections - 1) {
2800                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2801                    next[i] |= ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i] << 1)) |
2802                            ((data[i - ySections + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i + ySections] << 1)) |
2803                            ((data[i + ySections + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i - ySections] << 1)) ;
2804                }
2805            }
2806            else
2807            {
2808                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2809                    next[i] |= (data[i] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L)
2810                            | (data[i - ySections] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L) | (data[i + ySections] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L);
2811                }
2812
2813            }
2814        }
2815
2816        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
2817            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
2818                next[a] &= yEndMask;
2819            }
2820        }
2821        data = next;
2822        tallied = false;
2823        return this;
2824    }
2825    /**
2826     * Takes the pairs of "on" cells in this GreasedRegion that are separated by exactly one cell in an orthogonal or
2827     * diagonal line, and changes the gap cells to "on" as well. As a special case, this requires diagonals to either
2828     * have no "on" cells adjacent along the perpendicular diagonal, or both cells on that perpendicular diagonal need
2829     * to be "on." This is useful to counteract some less-desirable behavior of {@link #connect8way()}, where a right
2830     * angle would always get the inner corners filled because it was considered a diagonal.
2831     * <br>
2832     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
2833     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
2834     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
2835     * @return this for chaining
2836     */
2837    public GreasedRegion connectLines()
2838    {
2839        if(width < 2 || ySections == 0)
2840            return this;
2841
2842        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
2843        System.arraycopy(data, 0, next, 0, width * ySections);
2844        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
2845            next[a] |= ((data[a] << 1) & (data[a] >>> 1)) | data[a+ySections] | (data[a+ySections] << 1) | (data[a+ySections] >>> 1);
2846            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= ((data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1) & (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1))
2847                    | data[(width-2) *ySections+a] | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] >>> 1);
2848
2849            for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2850                next[i] |= ((data[i] << 1) & (data[i] >>> 1)) | (data[i - ySections] & data[i + ySections])
2851                        | (((data[i - ySections] << 1) & (data[i + ySections] >>> 1))
2852                           ^ ((data[i + ySections] << 1) & (data[i - ySections] >>> 1)));
2853            }
2854
2855            if(a > 0) {
2856                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2857                    next[i] |= ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i] >>> 1))
2858                            | (((data[i - ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i + ySections] >>> 1))
2859                               ^ ((data[i + ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i - ySections] >>> 1)));
2860                }
2861            }
2862            else
2863            {
2864                for (int i = ySections; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2865                    next[i] |= (data[i] >>> 1 & 1L) | (data[i - ySections] >>> 1 & 1L) | (data[i + ySections] >>> 1 & 1L);
2866                }
2867            }
2868
2869            if(a < ySections - 1) {
2870                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2871                    next[i] |= ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i] << 1))
2872                            | (((data[i - ySections + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i + ySections] << 1))
2873                               ^ ((data[i + ySections + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i - ySections] << 1)));
2874                }
2875            }
2876            else
2877            {
2878                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2879                    next[i] |= (data[i] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L)
2880                            | (data[i - ySections] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L) | (data[i + ySections] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L);
2881                }
2882
2883            }
2884        }
2885
2886        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
2887            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
2888                next[a] &= yEndMask;
2889            }
2890        }
2891        data = next;
2892        tallied = false;
2893        return this;
2894    }
2895
2896    /**
2897     * Like {@link #retract()}, this reduces the width of thick areas of this GreasedRegion, but thin() will not remove
2898     * areas that would be identical in a subsequent call to retract(), such as if the area would be eliminated. This
2899     * is useful primarily for adjusting areas so they do not exceed a width of 2 cells, though their length (the longer
2900     * of the two dimensions) will be unaffected by this. Especially wide, irregularly-shaped areas may have unintended
2901     * appearances if you call this repeatedly or use {@link #thinFully()}; consider using this sparingly, or primarily
2902     * when an area has just gotten thicker than desired.
2903     * <br>
2904     * This currently uses 4-way adjacency, but had previously used 8-way; if you want the behavior this previously had,
2905     * you can use {@link #thin8way()}, but it may be a good idea to try this method as well (some of the old behavior
2906     * had problems where it yielded significantly larger minimum widths in some areas).
2907     * @return this for chaining
2908     */
2909    public GreasedRegion thin()
2910    {
2911        if(width <= 2 || ySections <= 0)
2912            return this;
2913        GreasedRegion c1 = new GreasedRegion(this).retract(),
2914                c2 = new GreasedRegion(c1).expand().xor(this).expand().and(this);
2915        remake(c1).or(c2);
2916        /*
2917        System.out.println("\n\nc1:\n" + c1.toString() + "\n");
2918        System.out.println("\n\nc2:\n" + c2.toString() + "\n");
2919        System.out.println("\n\nthis:\n" + toString() + "\n");
2920        */
2921        return this;
2922    }
2923
2924    /**
2925     * Calls {@link #thin()} repeatedly, until the result is unchanged from the last call. Consider using the idiom
2926     * {@code expand8way().retract().thinFully()} to help change a possibly-strange appearance when the GreasedRegion
2927     * this is called on touches the edges of the grid. In general, this method is likely to go too far when it tries to
2928     * thin a round or irregular area, and this often results in many diagonal lines spanning the formerly-thick area.
2929     * <br>
2930     * This currently uses 4-way adjacency, but had previously used 8-way; if you want the behavior this previously had,
2931     * you can use {@link #thinFully8way()}, but it may be a good idea to try this method as well (some of the old
2932     * behavior had problems where it yielded significantly larger minimum widths in some areas).
2933     * @return this for chaining
2934     */
2935    public GreasedRegion thinFully()
2936    {
2937        while (size() != thin().size());
2938        return this;
2939    }
2940
2941
2942    /**
2943     * Like {@link #retract8way()}, this reduces the width of thick areas of this GreasedRegion, but thin8way() will not
2944     * remove areas that would be identical in a subsequent call to retract8way(), such as if the area would be
2945     * eliminated. This is useful primarily for adjusting areas so they do not exceed a width of 2 cells, though their
2946     * length (the longer of the two dimensions) will be unaffected by this. Especially wide, irregularly-shaped areas
2947     * may have unintended appearances if you call this repeatedly or use {@link #thinFully8way()}; consider using this
2948     * sparingly, or primarily when an area has just gotten thicker than desired.
2949     * <br>
2950     * This method was called {@link #thin()}, but now that name refers to a variant that uses 4-way adjacency.
2951     * @return this for chaining
2952     */
2953    public GreasedRegion thin8way()
2954    {
2955        if(width <= 2 || ySections <= 0)
2956            return this;
2957        GreasedRegion c1 = new GreasedRegion(this).retract8way(),
2958                c2 = new GreasedRegion(c1).expand8way().xor(this).expand8way().and(this);
2959        remake(c1).or(c2);
2960        return this;
2961    }
2962
2963    /**
2964     * Calls {@link #thin8way()} repeatedly, until the result is unchanged from the last call. Consider using the idiom
2965     * {@code expand8way().retract().thinFully8way()} to help change a strange appearance when the GreasedRegion this is
2966     * called on touches the edges of the grid. In general, this method is likely to go too far when it tries to thin a
2967     * round or irregular area, and this often results in many diagonal lines spanning the formerly-thick area.
2968     * <br>
2969     * This method was called {@link #thinFully()}, but now that name refers to a variant that uses 4-way adjacency.
2970     * @return this for chaining
2971     */
2972    public GreasedRegion thinFully8way()
2973    {
2974        while (size() != thin8way().size());
2975        return this;
2976    }
2977
2978
2979    /**
2980     * Removes "on" cells that are orthogonally adjacent to other "on" cells, keeping at least one cell in a group "on."
2981     * Uses a "checkerboard" pattern to determine which cells to turn  off, with all cells that would be black on a
2982     * checkerboard turned off and all others kept as-is.
2983     * @return this for chaining
2984     */
2985    public GreasedRegion disperse()
2986    {
2987        if(width < 1 || ySections <= 0)
2988            return this;
2989        long mask = 0x5555555555555555L;
2990        for (int i = 0; i < width; i++) {
2991            for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
2992                data[j] &= mask;
2993            }
2994            mask = ~mask;
2995        }
2996        tallied = false;
2997        return this;
2998    }
2999    /**
3000     * Removes "on" cells that are 8-way adjacent to other "on" cells, keeping at least one cell in a group "on."
3001     * Uses a "grid-like" pattern to determine which cells to turn off, with all cells with even x and even y kept as-is
3002     * but all other cells (with either or both odd x or odd y) turned off.
3003     * @return this for chaining
3004     */
3005    public GreasedRegion disperse8way()
3006    {
3007        if(width < 1 || ySections <= 0)
3008            return this;
3009        int len = data.length;
3010        long mask = 0x5555555555555555L;
3011        for (int j = 0; j < len - 1; j += 2) {
3012            data[j] &= mask;
3013            data[j+1] = 0;
3014        }
3015        tallied = false;
3016        return this;
3017    }
3018    /**
3019     * Removes "on" cells that are nearby other "on" cells, with a random factor to which bits are actually turned off
3020     * that still ensures exactly half of the bits are kept as-is (the one exception is when height is an odd number,
3021     * which makes the bottom row slightly random).
3022     * @param random the RNG used for a random factor
3023     * @return this for chaining
3024     */
3025    public GreasedRegion disperseRandom(RandomnessSource random)
3026    {
3027        if(width < 1 || ySections <= 0)
3028            return this;
3029        int len = data.length;
3030        for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
3031            data[j] &= randomInterleave(random);
3032        }
3033        tallied = false;
3034        return this;
3035    }
3036    /**
3037     * Generates a random 64-bit long with a number of '1' bits (Hamming weight) equal on average to bitCount.
3038     * For example, calling this with a parameter of 32 will be equivalent to calling nextLong() on the given
3039     * RandomnessSource, which could be an {@link RNG} or any RandomnessSource with good 64-bit generation quality.
3040     * Calling this with a parameter of 16 will have on average 16 of the 64 bits in the returned long set to '1',
3041     * distributed pseudo-randomly, while a parameter of 47 will have on average 47 bits set. This can be useful for
3042     * certain code that uses bits to represent data but needs a different ratio of set bits to unset bits than 1:1.
3043     * <br>
3044     * The parameter {@code random} can be an object like a {@link DiverRNG}, an {@link RNG} backed by a
3045     * well-distributed RandomnessSource like its default, DiverRNG, a {@link GWTRNG} (especially if you target GWT,
3046     * where it will perform much better than most alternatives), or any of various other RandomnessSource
3047     * implementations that distribute bits well for {@link RandomnessSource#nextLong()}, but should not be
3048     * intentionally-biased RNGs like {@link DharmaRNG} or {@link EditRNG}, nor double-based QRNGs like
3049     * {@link VanDerCorputQRNG} or {@link SobolQRNG}.
3050     * @param random used to determine random factors; likely to be an {@link RNG}, {@link DiverRNG}, or {@link GWTRNG}
3051     * @param bitCount an int, only considered if between 0 and 64, that is the average number of bits to set
3052     * @return a 64-bit long that, on average, should have bitCount bits set to 1, potentially anywhere in the long
3053     */
3054    public static long approximateBits(RandomnessSource random, int bitCount) {
3055        if (bitCount <= 0)
3056            return 0L;
3057        if (bitCount >= 64)
3058            return -1L;
3059        if (bitCount == 32)
3060            return random.nextLong();
3061        boolean high = bitCount > 32;
3062        int altered = (high ? 64 - bitCount : bitCount), lsb = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(altered);
3063        long data = random.nextLong();
3064        for (int i = lsb << 1; i <= 16; i <<= 1) {
3065            if ((altered & i) == 0)
3066                data &= random.nextLong();
3067            else
3068                data |= random.nextLong();
3069        }
3070        return high ? ~(random.nextLong() & data) : (random.nextLong() & data);
3071    }
3072
3073    /**
3074     * Gets a somewhat-random long with exactly 32 bits set; in each pair of bits starting at bit 0 and bit 1, then bit
3075     * 2 and bit 3, up to bit 62 and bit 3, one bit will be 1 and one bit will be 0 in each pair.
3076     * <br>
3077     * Not exactly general-use; meant for generating data for GreasedRegion.
3078     * @return a random long with 32 "1" bits, distributed so exactly one bit is "1" for each pair of bits
3079     */
3080    public static long randomInterleave(RandomnessSource random) {
3081        long bits = random.nextLong() & 0xFFFFFFFFL, ib = ~bits & 0xFFFFFFFFL;
3082        bits |= (bits << 16);
3083        ib |= (ib << 16);
3084        bits &= 0x0000FFFF0000FFFFL;
3085        ib &= 0x0000FFFF0000FFFFL;
3086        bits |= (bits << 8);
3087        ib |= (ib << 8);
3088        bits &= 0x00FF00FF00FF00FFL;
3089        ib &= 0x00FF00FF00FF00FFL;
3090        bits |= (bits << 4);
3091        ib |= (ib << 4);
3092        bits &= 0x0F0F0F0F0F0F0F0FL;
3093        ib &= 0x0F0F0F0F0F0F0F0FL;
3094        bits |= (bits << 2);
3095        ib |= (ib << 2);
3096        bits &= 0x3333333333333333L;
3097        ib &= 0x3333333333333333L;
3098        bits |= (bits << 1);
3099        ib |= (ib << 1);
3100        bits &= 0x5555555555555555L;
3101        ib &= 0x5555555555555555L;
3102        return (bits | (ib << 1));
3103    }

3105    /**
3106     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and expands them by one cell in the 4 orthogonal directions, making
3107     * each "on" cell take up a plus-shaped area that may overlap with other "on" cells (which is just a normal "on"
3108     * cell then).
3109     * <br>
3110     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3111     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3112     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
3113     * @return this for chaining
3114     */
3115    public GreasedRegion expand()
3116    {
3117        if(width < 2 || ySections == 0)
3118            return this;
3119
3120        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3121        System.arraycopy(data, 0, next, 0, width * ySections);
3122        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
3123            next[a] |= (data[a] << 1) | (data[a] >>> 1) | data[a+ySections];
3124            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1) | data[(width-2) *ySections+a];
3125
3126            for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3127                next[i] |= (data[i] << 1) | (data[i] >>> 1) | data[i - ySections] | data[i + ySections];
3128            }
3129
3130            if(a > 0) {
3131                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3132                    next[i] |= (data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63;
3133                }
3134            }
3135
3136            if(a < ySections - 1) {
3137                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3138                    next[i] |= (data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63;
3139                }
3140            }
3141        }
3142
3143        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
3144            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3145                next[a] &= yEndMask;
3146            }
3147        }
3148        data = next;
3149        tallied = false;
3150        return this;
3151    }
3152    /**
3153     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and expands them by amount cells in the 4 orthogonal directions,
3154     * making each "on" cell take up a plus-shaped area that may overlap with other "on" cells (which is just a normal
3155     * "on" cell then).
3156     * <br>
3157     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3158     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3159     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
3160     * @return this for chaining
3161     */
3162    @Override
3163    public GreasedRegion expand(int amount)
3164    {
3165        for (int i = 0; i < amount; i++) {
3166            expand();
3167        }
3168        return this;
3169    }
3170    /**
3171     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and produces amount GreasedRegions, each one expanded by 1 cell in
3172     * the 4 orthogonal directions relative to the previous GreasedRegion, making each "on" cell take up a plus-shaped
3173     * area that may overlap with other "on" cells (which is just a normal "on" cell then). This returns an array of
3174     * GreasedRegions with progressively greater expansions, and does not modify this GreasedRegion.
3175     * <br>
3176     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3177     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3178     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
3179     * @return an array of new GreasedRegions, length == amount, where each one is expanded by 1 relative to the last
3180     */
3181    public GreasedRegion[] expandSeries(int amount)
3182    {
3183        if(amount <= 0) return new GreasedRegion[0];
3184        GreasedRegion[] regions = new GreasedRegion[amount];
3185        GreasedRegion temp = new GreasedRegion(this);
3186        for (int i = 0; i < amount; i++) {
3187            regions[i] = new GreasedRegion(temp.expand());
3188        }
3189        return regions;
3190    }

3201    /**
3202     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and expands them by one cell in the 4 orthogonal directions, producing
3203     * a diamoond shape, then removes the original area before expansion, producing only the cells that were "off" in
3204     * this and within 1 cell (orthogonal-only) of an "on" cell. This method is similar to {@link #surface()}, but
3205     * surface finds cells inside the current GreasedRegion, while fringe finds cells outside it.
3206     * <br>
3207     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3208     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3209     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time. The surface and fringe methods do allocate one
3210     * temporary GreasedRegion to store the original before modification, but the others generally don't.
3211     * @return this for chaining
3212     */
3213    public GreasedRegion fringe()
3214    {
3215        GreasedRegion cpy = new GreasedRegion(this);
3216        expand();
3217        return andNot(cpy);
3218    }
3219    /**
3220     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and expands them by amount cells in the 4 orthogonal directions
3221     * (iteratively, producing a diamond shape), then removes the original area before expansion, producing only the
3222     * cells that were "off" in this and within amount cells (orthogonal-only) of an "on" cell. This method is similar
3223     * to {@link #surface()}, but surface finds cells inside the current GreasedRegion, while fringe finds cells outside
3224     * it.
3225     * <br>
3226     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3227     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3228     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time. The surface and fringe methods do allocate one
3229     * temporary GreasedRegion to store the original before modification, but the others generally don't.
3230     * @return this for chaining
3231     */
3232

3240    /**
3241     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and produces amount GreasedRegions, each one expanded by 1 cell in
3242     * the 4 orthogonal directions relative to the previous GreasedRegion, making each "on" cell take up a diamond-
3243     * shaped area. After producing the expansions, this removes the previous GreasedRegion from the next GreasedRegion
3244     * in the array, making each "fringe" in the series have 1 "thickness," which can be useful for finding which layer
3245     * of expansion a cell lies in. This returns an array of GreasedRegions with progressively greater expansions
3246     * without the cells of this GreasedRegion, and does not modify this GreasedRegion.
3247     * <br>
3248     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3249     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3250     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
3251     * @return an array of new GreasedRegions, length == amount, where each one is a 1-depth fringe pushed further out from this
3252     */
3253    public GreasedRegion[] fringeSeries(int amount)
3254    {
3255        if(amount <= 0) return new GreasedRegion[0];
3256        GreasedRegion[] regions = new GreasedRegion[amount];
3257        GreasedRegion temp = new GreasedRegion(this);
3258        regions[0] = new GreasedRegion(temp);
3259        for (int i = 1; i < amount; i++) {
3260            regions[i] = new GreasedRegion(temp.expand());
3261        }
3262        for (int i = 0; i < amount - 1; i++) {
3263            regions[i].xor(regions[i + 1]);
3264        }
3265        regions[amount - 1].fringe();
3266        return regions;
3267    }
3268    public ArrayList<GreasedRegion> fringeSeriesToLimit()
3269    {
3270        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> regions = expandSeriesToLimit();
3271        for (int i = regions.size() - 1; i > 0; i--) {
3272            regions.get(i).xor(regions.get(i-1));
3273        }
3274        regions.get(0).xor(this);
3275        return regions;
3276    }

3278    /**
3279     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and retracts them by one cell in the 4 orthogonal directions,
3280     * making each "on" cell that was orthogonally adjacent to an "off" cell into an "off" cell.
3281     * <br>
3282     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3283     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3284     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
3285     * @return this for chaining
3286     */
3287    public GreasedRegion retract()
3288    {
3289        if(width <= 2 || ySections <= 0)
3290            return this;
3291
3292        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3293        System.arraycopy(data, ySections, next, ySections, (width - 2) * ySections);
3294        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
3295            if(a > 0 && a < ySections - 1) {
3296                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3297                    next[i] &= ((data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3298                            & ((data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63))
3299                            & data[i - ySections]
3300                            & data[i + ySections];
3301                }
3302            }
3303            else if(a > 0) {
3304                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3305                    next[i] &= ((data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3306                            & (data[i] >>> 1)
3307                            & data[i - ySections]
3308                            & data[i + ySections];
3309                }
3310            }
3311            else if(a < ySections - 1) {
3312                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3313                    next[i] &= (data[i] << 1)
3314                            & ((data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63))
3315                            & data[i - ySections]
3316                            & data[i + ySections];
3317                }
3318            }
3319            else // only the case when ySections == 1
3320            {
3321                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3322                    next[i] &= (data[i] << 1) & (data[i] >>> 1) & data[i - ySections] & data[i + ySections];
3323                }
3324            }
3325        }
3326
3327        if(yEndMask != -1) {
3328            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3329                next[a] &= yEndMask;
3330            }
3331        }
3332        data = next;
3333        tallied = false;
3334        return this;
3335    }

3339     * this iteeratively amount times, making each "on" cell that was within amount orthogonal distance to an "off" cell
3340     * into an "off" cell.
3341     * <br>
3342     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3343     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3344     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.

3346     */

3348    {
3349        for (int i = 0; i < amount; i++) {
3350            retract();

3403    public ArrayList<GreasedRegion> surfaceSeriesToLimit()
3404    {
3405        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> regions = retractSeriesToLimit();
3406        if(regions.isEmpty())
3407            return regions;
3408        regions.add(0, regions.get(0).copy().xor(this));
3409        for (int i = 1; i < regions.size() - 1; i++) {
3410            regions.get(i).xor(regions.get(i+1));
3411        }
3412        return regions;

3414    public GreasedRegion expand8way()
3415    {
3416        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0)
3417            return this;
3418
3419        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3420        System.arraycopy(data, 0, next, 0, width * ySections);
3421        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
3422            next[a] |= (data[a] << 1) | (data[a] >>> 1)
3423                    | data[a+ySections] | (data[a+ySections] << 1) | (data[a+ySections] >>> 1);
3424            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1)
3425                    | data[(width-2) *ySections+a] | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] >>> 1);
3426
3427            for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3428                next[i] |= (data[i] << 1) | (data[i] >>> 1)
3429                        | data[i - ySections] | (data[i - ySections] << 1) | (data[i - ySections] >>> 1)
3430                        | data[i + ySections] | (data[i + ySections] << 1) | (data[i + ySections] >>> 1);
3431            }
3432
3433            if(a > 0) {
3434                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3435                    next[i] |= ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63) |
3436                            ((data[i - ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63) |
3437                            ((data[i + ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63);
3438                }
3439            }
3440
3441            if(a < ySections - 1) {
3442                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3443                    next[i] |= ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63) |
3444                            ((data[i - ySections + 1] & 1L) << 63) |
3445                            ((data[i + ySections+ 1] & 1L) << 63);
3446                }
3447            }
3448        }
3449
3450        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
3451            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3452                next[a] &= yEndMask;
3453            }
3454        }
3455        data = next;
3456        tallied = false;
3457        return this;
3458    }

3527    public GreasedRegion retract8way()
3528    {
3529        if(width <= 2 || ySections <= 0)
3530            return this;
3531
3532        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3533        System.arraycopy(data, ySections, next, ySections, (width - 2) * ySections);
3534        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
3535            if(a > 0 && a < ySections - 1) {
3536                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3537                    next[i] &= ((data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3538                            & ((data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63))
3539                            & data[i - ySections]
3540                            & data[i + ySections]
3541                            & ((data[i - ySections] << 1) | ((data[i - 1 - ySections] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3542                            & ((data[i + ySections] << 1) | ((data[i - 1 + ySections] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3543                            & ((data[i - ySections] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1 - ySections] & 1L) << 63))
3544                            & ((data[i + ySections] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1 + ySections] & 1L) << 63));
3545                }
3546            }
3547            else if(a > 0) {
3548                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3549                    next[i] &= ((data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3550                            & (data[i] >>> 1)
3551                            & data[i - ySections]
3552                            & data[i + ySections]
3553                            & ((data[i - ySections] << 1) | ((data[i - 1 - ySections] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3554                            & ((data[i + ySections] << 1) | ((data[i - 1 + ySections] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3555                            & (data[i - ySections] >>> 1)
3556                            & (data[i + ySections] >>> 1);
3557                }
3558            }
3559            else if(a < ySections - 1) {
3560                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3561                    next[i] &= (data[i] << 1)
3562                            & ((data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63))
3563                            & data[i - ySections]
3564                            & data[i + ySections]
3565                            & (data[i - ySections] << 1)
3566                            & (data[i + ySections] << 1)
3567                            & ((data[i - ySections] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1 - ySections] & 1L) << 63))
3568                            & ((data[i + ySections] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1 + ySections] & 1L) << 63));
3569                }
3570            }
3571            else // only the case when ySections == 1
3572            {
3573                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3574                    next[i] &= (data[i] << 1)
3575                            & (data[i] >>> 1)
3576                            & data[i - ySections]
3577                            & data[i + ySections]
3578                            & (data[i - ySections] << 1)
3579                            & (data[i + ySections] << 1)
3580                            & (data[i - ySections] >>> 1)
3581                            & (data[i + ySections] >>> 1);
3582                }
3583            }
3584        }
3585
3586        if(yEndMask != -1) {
3587            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3588                next[a] &= yEndMask;
3589            }
3590        }
3591        data = next;
3592        tallied = false;
3593        return this;
3594    }

3600        }

3602    }

3637    public GreasedRegion[] surfaceSeries8way(int amount)
3638    {
3639        if(amount <= 0) return new GreasedRegion[0];
3640        GreasedRegion[] regions = new GreasedRegion[amount];
3641        GreasedRegion temp = new GreasedRegion(this);
3642        regions[0] = new GreasedRegion(temp);
3643        for (int i = 1; i < amount; i++) {
3644            regions[i] = new GreasedRegion(temp.retract8way());
3645        }
3646        for (int i = 0; i < amount - 1; i++) {
3647            regions[i].xor(regions[i + 1]);
3648        }
3649        regions[amount - 1].surface8way();
3650        return regions;
3651    }
3652    public ArrayList<GreasedRegion> surfaceSeriesToLimit8way()
3653    {
3654        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> regions = retractSeriesToLimit8way();
3655        if(regions.isEmpty())
3656            return regions;
3657        regions.add(0, regions.get(0).copy().xor(this));
3658        for (int i = 1; i < regions.size() - 1; i++) {
3659            regions.get(i).xor(regions.get(i+1));
3660        }
3661        return regions;
3662    }
3663    public GreasedRegion flood(GreasedRegion bounds)
3664    {
3665        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0 || bounds == null || bounds.width < 2 || bounds.ySections <= 0)
3666            return this;
3667
3668        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3669        for (int a = 0; a < ySections && a < bounds.ySections; a++) {
3670            next[a] |= (data[a] |(data[a] << 1) | (data[a] >>> 1) | data[a+ySections]) & bounds.data[a];
3671            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] | (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1)
3672                    | (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1) | data[(width-2) *ySections+a]) & bounds.data[(width-1)*bounds.ySections+a];
3673
3674            for (int i = ySections+a, j = bounds.ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections &&
3675                    j < (bounds.width - 1) * bounds.ySections; i+= ySections, j+= bounds.ySections) {
3676                next[i] |= (data[i] | (data[i] << 1) | (data[i] >>> 1) | data[i - ySections] | data[i + ySections]) & bounds.data[j];
3677            }
3678
3679            if(a > 0) {
3680                for (int i = ySections+a, j = bounds.ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections && j < (bounds.width-1) * bounds.ySections;
3681                     i+= ySections, j += bounds.ySections) {
3682                    next[i] |= (data[i] | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63)) & bounds.data[j];
3683                }
3684            }
3685
3686            if(a < ySections - 1 && a < bounds.ySections - 1) {
3687                for (int i = ySections+a, j = bounds.ySections+a;
3688                     i < (width-1) * ySections && j < (bounds.width-1) * bounds.ySections; i+= ySections, j += bounds.ySections) {
3689                    next[i] |= (data[i] | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63)) & bounds.data[j];
3690                }
3691            }
3692        }
3693
3694        if(yEndMask != -1 && bounds.yEndMask != -1) {
3695            if(ySections == bounds.ySections) {
3696                long mask = ((yEndMask >>> 1) <= (bounds.yEndMask >>> 1))
3697                        ? yEndMask : bounds.yEndMask;
3698                for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3699                    next[a] &= mask;
3700                }
3701            }
3702            else if(ySections < bounds.ySections) {
3703                for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3704                    next[a] &= yEndMask;
3705                }
3706            }
3707            else {
3708                for (int a = bounds.ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3709                    next[a] &= bounds.yEndMask;
3710                }
3711            }
3712        }
3713        data = next;
3714        tallied = false;
3715        return this;
3716    }
3717

3720        int ct = size(), ct2;

3722            flood(bounds);
3723            if(ct == (ct2 = size()))
3724                break;
3725            else
3726                ct = ct2;
3727
3728        }
3729        return this;
3730    }
