3770    public GreasedRegion flood8way(GreasedRegion bounds)
3771    {
3772        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0 || bounds == null || bounds.width < 2 || bounds.ySections <= 0)
3773            return this;
3774
3775        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3776        for (int a = 0; a < ySections && a < bounds.ySections; a++) {
3777            next[a] |= (data[a] | (data[a] << 1) | (data[a] >>> 1)
3778                    | data[a+ySections] | (data[a+ySections] << 1) | (data[a+ySections] >>> 1)) & bounds.data[a];
3779            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= (data[(width-1)*ySections+a]
3780                    | (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1)
3781                    | data[(width-2) *ySections+a] | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] >>> 1))
3782                    & bounds.data[(width-1)*bounds.ySections+a];
3783
3784            for (int i = ySections+a, j = bounds.ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections &&
3785                    j < (bounds.width - 1) * bounds.ySections; i+= ySections, j+= bounds.ySections) {
3786                next[i] |= (data[i] | (data[i] << 1) | (data[i] >>> 1)
3787                        | data[i - ySections] | (data[i - ySections] << 1) | (data[i - ySections] >>> 1)
3788                        | data[i + ySections] | (data[i + ySections] << 1) | (data[i + ySections] >>> 1))
3789                        & bounds.data[j];
3790            }
3791
3792            if(a > 0) {
3793                for (int i = ySections+a, j = bounds.ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections && j < (bounds.width-1) * bounds.ySections;
3794                     i+= ySections, j += bounds.ySections) {
3795                    next[i] |= (data[i] | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63) |
3796                            ((data[i - ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63) |
3797                            ((data[i + ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63)) & bounds.data[j];
3798                }
3799            }
3800
3801            if(a < ySections - 1 && a < bounds.ySections - 1) {
3802                for (int i = ySections+a, j = bounds.ySections+a;
3803                     i < (width-1) * ySections && j < (bounds.width-1) * bounds.ySections; i+= ySections, j += bounds.ySections) {
3804                    next[i] |= (data[i] | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63) |
3805                            ((data[i - ySections + 1] & 1L) << 63) |
3806                            ((data[i + ySections+ 1] & 1L) << 63)) & bounds.data[j];
3807                }
3808            }
3809        }
3810
3811        if(yEndMask != -1 && bounds.yEndMask != -1) {
3812            if(ySections == bounds.ySections) {
3813                long mask = ((yEndMask >>> 1) <= (bounds.yEndMask >>> 1))
3814                        ? yEndMask : bounds.yEndMask;
3815                for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3816                    next[a] &= mask;
3817                }
3818            }
3819            else if(ySections < bounds.ySections) {
3820                for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3821                    next[a] &= yEndMask;
3822                }
3823            }
3824            else {
3825                for (int a = bounds.ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3826                    next[a] &= bounds.yEndMask;
3827                }
3828            }
3829        }
3830        data = next;
3831        tallied = false;
3832        return this;
3833    }

3883    public GreasedRegion spill(GreasedRegion bounds, int volume, IRNG rng)
3884    {
3885        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0 || bounds == null || bounds.width < 2 || bounds.ySections <= 0)
3886            return this;
3887        int current = size();
3888        if(current >= volume)
3889            return this;
3890        GreasedRegion t = new GreasedRegion(this).notAnd(bounds);
3891        long[] b2 = new long[t.data.length];
3892        System.arraycopy(t.data, 0, b2, 0, b2.length);
3893        t.remake(this).fringe().and(bounds).tally();
3894        if(t.ct <= 0)
3895            return this;
3896        Coord c;
3897        int x, y, p;
3898        for (int i = current; i < volume; i++) {
3899            c = t.singleRandom(rng);
3900            x = c.x;
3901            y = c.y;
3902            if(data[p = x * ySections + (y >> 6)] != (data[p] |= 1L << (y & 63)))
3903            {
3904                counts[p]++;
3905                for (int j = p+1; j < data.length; j++) {
3906                    if(counts[j] > 0) ++counts[j];
3907                }
3908                ct++;
3909                t.data[p] &= ~(1L << (y & 63));
3910//                b2[p] &= ~(1L << (y & 63));
3911                if(x < width - 1 && (b2[p = (x+1) * ySections + (y >> 6)] & 1L << (y & 63)) != 0)
3912                {
3913                    t.data[p] |= 1L << (y & 63);
3914                }
3915                if(y < height - 1 && (b2[p = x * ySections + (y+1 >> 6)] & 1L << (y+1 & 63)) != 0)
3916                {
3917                    t.data[p] |= 1L << (y+1 & 63);
3918                }
3919                if(y > 0 && (b2[p = x * ySections + (y-1 >> 6)] & 1L << (y-1 & 63)) != 0)
3920                {
3921                    t.data[p] |= 1L << (y-1 & 63);
3922                }
3923                if(x > 0 && (b2[p = (x-1) * ySections + (y >> 6)] & 1L << (y & 63)) != 0)
3924                {
3925
3926                    t.data[p] |= 1L << (y & 63);
3927                }
3928                t.tally();
3929                if(t.ct <= 0) break;
3930            }
3931        }
3932        tallied = false;
3933        return this;
3934    }
3935
3936    public GreasedRegion removeCorners()
3937    {
3938        if(width <= 2 || ySections <= 0)
3939            return this;
3940
3941        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3942        System.arraycopy(data, 0, next, 0, width * ySections);
3943        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
3944            if(a > 0 && a < ySections - 1) {
3945                next[a] &= (((data[a] << 1) | ((data[a - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3946                        & ((data[a] >>> 1) | ((data[a + 1] & 1L) << 63)));
3947                next[(width - 1) * ySections + a] &= (((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a] << 1)
3948                        | ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3949                        & ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a] >>> 1)
3950                        | ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a + 1] & 1L) << 63)));
3951                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3952                    next[i] &= (((data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3953                            & ((data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63)))
3954                            | (data[i - ySections]
3955                            & data[i + ySections]);
3956                }
3957            }
3958            else if(a > 0) {
3959                next[a] &= (((data[a] << 1) | ((data[a - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3960                        & (data[a] >>> 1));
3961                next[(width - 1) * ySections + a] &= (((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a] << 1)
3962                        | ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3963                        & (data[(width - 1) * ySections + a] >>> 1));
3964                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3965                    next[i] &= (((data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3966                            & (data[i] >>> 1))
3967                            | (data[i - ySections]
3968                            & data[i + ySections]);
3969                }
3970            }
3971            else if(a < ySections - 1) {
3972                next[a] &= ((data[a] << 1)
3973                        & ((data[a] >>> 1)
3974                        | ((data[a + 1] & 1L) << 63)));
3975                next[(width - 1) * ySections + a] &= ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a] << 1)
3976                        & ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a] >>> 1)
3977                        | ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a + 1] & 1L) << 63)));
3978                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3979                    next[i] &= ((data[i] << 1)
3980                            & ((data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63)))
3981                            | (data[i - ySections]
3982                            & data[i + ySections]);
3983                }
3984            }
3985            else // only the case when ySections == 1
3986            {
3987                next[0] &= (data[0] << 1) & (data[0] >>> 1);
3988                next[width-1] &= (data[width-1] << 1) & (data[width-1] >>> 1);
3989                for (int i = 1+a; i < (width - 1); i++) {
3990                    next[i] &= ((data[i] << 1) & (data[i] >>> 1)) | (data[i - ySections] & data[i + ySections]);
3991                }
3992            }
3993        }
3994
3995        if(yEndMask != -1) {
3996            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3997                next[a] &= yEndMask;
3998            }
3999        }
4000        data = next;
4001        tallied = false;
4002        return this;
4003    }
4004
4005    /**
4006     * If this GreasedRegion stores multiple unconnected "on" areas, this finds each isolated area (areas that
4007     * are only adjacent diagonally are considered separate from each other) and returns it as an element in an
4008     * ArrayList of GreasedRegion, with one GreasedRegion per isolated area. Not to be confused with
4009     * {@link #split8way()}, which considers diagonally-adjacent cells as part of one region, while this method requires
4010     * cells to be orthogonally adjacent.
4011     * <br>
4012     * Useful when you have, for example, all the rooms in a dungeon with their connecting corridors removed, but want
4013     * to separate the rooms. You can get the aforementioned data assuming a bare dungeon called map using:
4014     * <br>
4015     * {@code GreasedRegion floors = new GreasedRegion(map, '.'),
4016     * rooms = floors.copy().retract8way().flood(floors, 2),
4017     * corridors = floors.copy().andNot(rooms),
4018     * doors = rooms.copy().and(corridors.copy().fringe());}
4019     * <br>
4020     * You can then get all rooms as separate regions with {@code List<GreasedRegion> apart = split(rooms);}, or
4021     * substitute {@code split(corridors)} to get the corridors. The room-finding technique works by shrinking floors
4022     * by a radius of 1 (8-way), which causes thin areas like corridors of 2 or less width to be removed, then
4023     * flood-filling the floors out from the area that produces by 2 cells (4-way this time) to restore the original
4024     * size of non-corridor areas (plus some extra to ensure odd shapes are kept). Corridors are obtained by removing
4025     * the rooms from floors. The example code also gets the doors (which overlap with rooms, not corridors) by finding
4026     * where the a room and a corridor are adjacent. This technique is used with some enhancements in the RoomFinder
4027     * class.
4028     * @see squidpony.squidgrid.mapping.RoomFinder for a class that uses this technique without exposing GreasedRegion
4029     * @return an ArrayList containing each unconnected area from packed as a GreasedRegion element
4030     */
4031    public ArrayList<GreasedRegion> split()
4032    {
4033        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> scattered = new ArrayList<>(32);
4034        int fst = firstTight();
4035        GreasedRegion remaining = new GreasedRegion(this);
4036        while (fst >= 0) {
4037            GreasedRegion filled = new GreasedRegion(width, height).insert(fst).flood(remaining, width * height);
4038            scattered.add(filled);
4039            remaining.andNot(filled);
4040            fst = remaining.firstTight();
4041        }
4042        return scattered;
4043    }
4044    /**
4045     * If this GreasedRegion stores multiple unconnected "on" areas, this finds each isolated area (areas that
4046     * are only adjacent diagonally are considered <b>one area</b> with this) and returns it as an element in an
4047     * ArrayList of GreasedRegion, with one GreasedRegion per isolated area. This should not be confused with
4048     * {@link #split()}, which is almost identical except that split() considers only orthogonal connections, while this
4049     * method considers both orthogonal and diagonal connections between cells as joining an area.
4050     * <br>
4051     * Useful when you have, for example, all the rooms in a dungeon with their connecting corridors removed, but want
4052     * to separate the rooms. You can get the aforementioned data assuming a bare dungeon called map using:
4053     * <br>
4054     * {@code GreasedRegion floors = new GreasedRegion(map, '.'),
4055     * rooms = floors.copy().retract8way().flood(floors, 2),
4056     * corridors = floors.copy().andNot(rooms),
4057     * doors = rooms.copy().and(corridors.copy().fringe());}
4058     * <br>
4059     * You can then get all rooms as separate regions with {@code List<GreasedRegion> apart = split(rooms);}, or
4060     * substitute {@code split(corridors)} to get the corridors. The room-finding technique works by shrinking floors
4061     * by a radius of 1 (8-way), which causes thin areas like corridors of 2 or less width to be removed, then
4062     * flood-filling the floors out from the area that produces by 2 cells (4-way this time) to restore the original
4063     * size of non-corridor areas (plus some extra to ensure odd shapes are kept). Corridors are obtained by removing
4064     * the rooms from floors. The example code also gets the doors (which overlap with rooms, not corridors) by finding
4065     * where the a room and a corridor are adjacent. This technique is used with some enhancements in the RoomFinder
4066     * class.
4067     * @see squidpony.squidgrid.mapping.RoomFinder for a class that uses this technique without exposing GreasedRegion
4068     * @return an ArrayList containing each unconnected area from packed as a GreasedRegion element
4069     */
4070    public ArrayList<GreasedRegion> split8way()
4071    {
4072        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> scattered = new ArrayList<>(32);
4073        int fst = firstTight();
4074        GreasedRegion remaining = new GreasedRegion(this);
4075        while (fst >= 0) {
4076            GreasedRegion filled = new GreasedRegion(width, height).insert(fst).flood8way(remaining, width * height);
4077            scattered.add(filled);
4078            remaining.andNot(filled);
4079            fst = remaining.firstTight();
4080        }
4081        return scattered;
4082    }
4083
4084    /**
4085     * Finds the largest contiguous area of "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and returns it; does not modify this
4086     * GreasedRegion. If there are multiple areas that are all equally large with no larger area, this returns the
4087     * region it checks first and still is largest (first determined by the same ordering {@link #nth(int)} takes).
4088     * This may return an empty GreasedRegion if there are no "on" cells, but it will never return null.
4089     * Here, contiguous means adjacent on an orthogonal direction, and this doesn't consider diagonally-connected cells
4090     * as contiguous unless they also have an orthogonal connection.
4091     * @return a new GreasedRegion that corresponds to the largest contiguous sub-region of "on" cells in this.
4092     */
4093    public GreasedRegion largestPart()
4094    {
4095        int fst = firstTight(), bestSize = 0, currentSize;
4096        GreasedRegion remaining = new GreasedRegion(this), filled = new GreasedRegion(width, height),
4097                choice = new GreasedRegion(width, height);
4098        while (fst >= 0) {
4099            filled.empty().insert(fst).flood(remaining, width * height);
4100            if((currentSize = filled.size()) > bestSize)
4101            {
4102                bestSize = currentSize;
4103                choice.remake(filled);
4104            }
4105            remaining.andNot(filled);
4106            fst = remaining.firstTight();
4107        }
4108        return choice;
4109    }
4110
4111    /**
4112     * Finds the largest contiguous area of "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and returns it; does not modify this
4113     * GreasedRegion. If there are multiple areas that are all equally large with no larger area, this returns the
4114     * region it checks first and still is largest (first determined by the same ordering {@link #nth(int)} takes).
4115     * This may return an empty GreasedRegion if there are no "on" cells, but it will never return null.
4116     * Here, contiguous means adjacent on any 8-way direction, and considers cells as part of a contiguous area even if
4117     * all connections but one, which can be orthogonal or diagonal, are blocked by "off" cells.
4118     * @return a new GreasedRegion that corresponds to the largest contiguous sub-region of "on" cells in this.
4119     */
4120    public GreasedRegion largestPart8way()
4121    {
4122        int fst = firstTight(), bestSize = 0, currentSize;
4123        GreasedRegion remaining = new GreasedRegion(this), filled = new GreasedRegion(width, height),
4124                choice = new GreasedRegion(width, height);
4125        while (fst >= 0) {
4126            filled.empty().insert(fst).flood8way(remaining, width * height);
4127            if((currentSize = filled.size()) > bestSize)
4128            {
4129                bestSize = currentSize;
4130                choice.remake(filled);
4131            }
4132            remaining.andNot(filled);
4133            fst = remaining.firstTight();
4134        }
4135        return choice;
4136    }

4138    /**
4139     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so the only cells that will be "on" have a neighbor upwards when this is called.
4140     * Up is defined as negative y. Neighbors are "on" cells exactly one cell away. A cell can have a neighbor
4141     * without itself being on; this is useful when finding the "shadow" cast away from "on" cells in one direction.
4142     * @return this, after modifications, for chaining
4143     */
4144    public GreasedRegion neighborUp()
4145    {
4146        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0)
4147            return this;
4148        for (int a = ySections - 1; a >= 0; a--) {
4149            if(a > 0) {
4150                for (int i = a; i < width * ySections; i+= ySections) {
4151                    data[i] = (data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63);
4152                }
4153            }
4154            else {
4155                for (int i = a; i < width * ySections; i+= ySections) {
4156                    data[i] = (data[i] << 1);
4157                }
4158            }
4159        }
4160        tallied = false;
4161        return this;
4162    }

4164    /**
4165     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so the only cells that will be "on" have a neighbor downwards when this is called.
4166     * Down is defined as positive y. Neighbors are "on" cells exactly one cell away. A cell can have a neighbor
4167     * without itself being on; this is useful when finding the "shadow" cast away from "on" cells in one direction.
4168     * @return this, after modifications, for chaining
4169     */
4170    public GreasedRegion neighborDown()
4171    {
4172        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0)
4173            return this;
4174        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
4175            if(a < ySections - 1) {
4176                for (int i = a; i < width * ySections; i+= ySections) {
4177                    data[i] = (data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63);
4178                }
4179            }
4180            else {
4181                for (int i = a; i < width * ySections; i+= ySections) {
4182                    data[i] = (data[i] >>> 1);
4183                }
4184            }
4185        }
4186        tallied = false;
4187        return this;
4188    }

4190    /**
4191     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so the only cells that will be "on" have a neighbor to the left when this is called.
4192     * Left is defined as negative x. Neighbors are "on" cells exactly one cell away. A cell can have a neighbor
4193     * without itself being on; this is useful when finding the "shadow" cast away from "on" cells in one direction.
4194     * @return this, after modifications, for chaining
4195     */
4196    public GreasedRegion neighborLeft()
4197    {
4198        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0)
4199            return this;
4200        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
4201            for (int i = ySections * (width - 1) + a; i >= ySections; i-= ySections) {
4202                data[i] = data[i - ySections];
4203            }
4204            data[a] = 0L;
4205        }
4206        tallied = false;
4207        return this;
4208    }

4219            return this;
4220        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
4221            for (int i = a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
4222                data[i] = data[i + ySections];
4223            }
4224            data[(width-1)*ySections+a] = 0L;
4225        }
4226        tallied = false;
4227        return this;
4228    }

4345    public GreasedRegion removeIsolated()
4346    {
4347        int fst = firstTight();
4348        GreasedRegion remaining = new GreasedRegion(this), filled = new GreasedRegion(this);
4349        while (fst >= 0) {
4350            filled.empty().insert(fst).flood(remaining, 8);
4351            if(filled.size() <= 4)
4352                andNot(filled);
4353            remaining.andNot(filled);
4354            fst = remaining.firstTight();
4355        }
4356        return this;
4357    }
4358
4359    /**
4360     * Returns true if any cell is "on" in both this GreasedRegion and in other; returns false otherwise. For example,
4361     * if (1,1) is "on" in this and (1,1) is "on" in other, this would return true, regardless of other cells.
4362     * @param other another GreasedRegion; its size does not have to match this GreasedRegion's size
4363     * @return true if this shares any "on" cells with other
4364     */
4365    public boolean intersects(GreasedRegion other)
4366    {
4367        if(other == null)
4368            return false;
4369        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < other.width; x++) {
4370            for (int y = 0; y < ySections && y < other.ySections; y++) {
4371                if((data[x * ySections + y] & other.data[x * ySections + y]) != 0)
4372                    return true;
4373            }
4374        }
4375        return false;
4376    }
4377
4378    public static OrderedSet<GreasedRegion> whichContain(int x, int y, GreasedRegion ... packed)
4379    {
4380        OrderedSet<GreasedRegion> found = new OrderedSet<>(packed.length);
4381        GreasedRegion tmp;
4382        for (int i = 0; i < packed.length; i++) {
4383            if((tmp = packed[i]) != null && tmp.contains(x, y))
4384                found.add(tmp);
4385        }
4386        return found;
4387    }
4388
4389    public static OrderedSet<GreasedRegion> whichContain(int x, int y, Collection<GreasedRegion> packed)
4390    {
4391        OrderedSet<GreasedRegion> found = new OrderedSet<>(packed.size());
4392        for (GreasedRegion tmp : packed) {
4393            if(tmp != null && tmp.contains(x, y))
4394                found.add(tmp);
4395        }
4396        return found;
4397    }

4400    public int size()
4401    {
4402        if(!tallied)
4403            tally();
4404        return ct;
4405    }
4406
4407    public Coord fit(double xFraction, double yFraction)
4408    {
4409        int tmp, xTotal = 0, yTotal = 0, xTarget, yTarget, bestX = -1;
4410        long t;
4411        int[] xCounts = new int[width];
4412        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4413            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4414                t = data[x * ySections + s] | 0L;
4415                if (t != 0) {
4416                    tmp = Long.bitCount(t);
4417                    xCounts[x] += tmp;
4418                    xTotal += tmp;
4419                }
4420            }
4421        }
4422        xTarget = (int)(xTotal * xFraction);
4423        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4424            if((xTarget -= xCounts[x]) < 0)
4425            {
4426                bestX = x;
4427                yTotal = xCounts[x];
4428                break;
4429            }
4430        }
4431        if(bestX < 0)
4432        {
4433            return Coord.get(-1, -1);
4434        }
4435        yTarget = (int)(yTotal * yFraction);
4436
4437        for (int s = 0, y = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4438            t = data[bestX * ySections + s] | 0L;
4439            for (long cy = 1L; cy != 0L && y < height; y++, cy <<= 1) {
4440                if((t & (cy | 0L)) != 0 && --yTarget < 0)
4441                {
4442                    return Coord.get(bestX, y);
4443                }
4444            }
4445        }
4446
4447        return Coord.get(-1, -1);
4448    }
4449
4450    public int[][] fit(int[][] basis, int defaultValue)
4451    {
4452        int[][] next = ArrayTools.fill(defaultValue, width, height);
4453        if(basis == null || basis.length <= 0 || basis[0] == null || basis[0].length <= 0)
4454            return next;
4455        int tmp, xTotal = 0, yTotal = 0, xTarget, yTarget, bestX, oX = basis.length, oY = basis[0].length, ao;
4456        long t;
4457        int[] xCounts = new int[width];
4458        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4459            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4460                t = data[x * ySections + s] | 0L;
4461                if (t != 0) {
4462                    tmp = Long.bitCount(t);
4463                    xCounts[x] += tmp;
4464                    xTotal += tmp;
4465                }
4466            }
4467        }
4468        if(xTotal <= 0)
4469            return next;
4470        for (int aX = 0; aX < oX; aX++) {
4471            CELL_WISE:
4472            for (int aY = 0; aY < oY; aY++) {
4473                if((ao = basis[aX][aY]) == defaultValue)
4474                    continue;
4475                xTarget = xTotal * aX / oX;
4476                for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4477                    if((xTarget -= xCounts[x]) < 0)
4478                    {
4479                        bestX = x;
4480                        yTotal = xCounts[x];
4481                        yTarget = yTotal * aY / oY;
4482                        for (int s = 0, y = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4483                            t = data[bestX * ySections + s] | 0L;
4484                            for (long cy = 1L; cy != 0L && y < height; y++, cy <<= 1) {
4485                                if((t & (cy|0L)) != 0 && --yTarget < 0)
4486                                {
4487                                    next[bestX][y] = ao;
4488                                    continue CELL_WISE;
4489                                }
4490                            }
4491                        }
4492                        continue CELL_WISE;
4493                    }
4494                }
4495
4496            }
4497        }
4498
4499        return next;
4500    }
4501    
4502    /**
4503     * Don't use this in new code; prefer {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double)}, {@link #quasiRandomSeparated(double)},
4504     * or {@link #separatedZCurve(double)}. This method has issues with being unable to fill the requested fraction, but
4505     * the others mentioned don't. See their documentation for what all these group of methods do.
4506     * @param fraction between 0.0 and 1.0
4507     * @return a Coord array that may not have the full fraction used; you have been advised
4508     */
4509    public Coord[] separatedPortion(double fraction)
4510    {
4511        if(fraction < 0)
4512            return new Coord[0];
4513        if(fraction > 1)
4514            fraction = 1;
4515        int ct, tmp, xTotal = 0, yTotal = 0, xTarget, yTarget, bestX = -1;
4516        long t;
4517        int[] xCounts = new int[width];
4518        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4519            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4520                t = data[x * ySections + s] | 0L;
4521                if (t != 0) {
4522                    tmp = Long.bitCount(t);
4523                    xCounts[x] += tmp;
4524                    xTotal += tmp;
4525                }
4526            }
4527        }
4528        Coord[] vl = new Coord[ct = (int)(fraction * xTotal)];
4529        double[] vec = new double[2];
4530        sobol.skipTo(1337);
4531        EACH_SOBOL:
4532        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++)
4533        {
4534            sobol.fillVector(vec);
4535            xTarget = (int) (xTotal * vec[0]);
4536            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4537                if ((xTarget -= xCounts[x]) < 0) {
4538                    bestX = x;
4539                    yTotal = xCounts[x];
4540                    break;
4541                }
4542            }
4543            yTarget = (int) (yTotal * vec[1]);
4544
4545            for (int s = 0, y = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4546                t = data[bestX * ySections + s] | 0L;
4547                for (long cy = 1L; cy != 0L && y < height; y++, cy <<= 1) {
4548                    if ((t & (cy|0L)) != 0 && --yTarget < 0) {
4549                        vl[i] = Coord.get(bestX, y);
4550                        continue EACH_SOBOL;
4551                    }
4552                }
4553            }
4554        }
4555        return vl;
4556
4557    }
4558    /**
4559     * Don't use this in new code; prefer {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double, int, long)} with a random long as the
4560     * last parameter. This method has issues with being unable to fill the requested fraction, but mixedRandomSeparated
4561     * does not. See its documentation for what this method is supposed to do.
4562     * @param fraction between 0.0 and 1.0
4563     * @param rng an IRNG that will be used to get a random starting point in the Sobol sequence this uses internally
4564     * @return a Coord array that may not have the full fraction used; you have been advised
4565     */
4566    public Coord[] randomSeparated(double fraction, IRNG rng)
4567    {
4568        return randomSeparated(fraction, rng, -1);
4569    }
4570    /**
4571     * Don't use this in new code; prefer {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double, int, long)} with a random long as the
4572     * last parameter. This method has issues with being unable to fill the requested fraction, but mixedRandomSeparated
4573     * does not. See its documentation for what this method is supposed to do.
4574     * @param fraction between 0.0 and 1.0
4575     * @param rng an IRNG that will be used to get a random starting point in the Sobol sequence this uses internally
4576     * @param limit how many Coord values this should return, at most; typically this will return less
4577     * @return a Coord array that may not have the full fraction used; you have been advised
4578     */
4579    public Coord[] randomSeparated(double fraction, IRNG rng, int limit)
4580    {
4581        if(fraction < 0)
4582            return new Coord[0];
4583        if(fraction > 1)
4584            fraction = 1;
4585        int ct, tmp, xTotal = 0, yTotal = 0, xTarget, yTarget, bestX = -1;
4586        long t;
4587        int[] xCounts = new int[width];
4588        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4589            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4590                t = data[x * ySections + s] | 0L;
4591                if (t != 0) {
4592                    tmp = Long.bitCount(t);
4593                    xCounts[x] += tmp;
4594                    xTotal += tmp;
4595                }
4596            }
4597        }
4598        ct = (int)(fraction * xTotal);
4599        if(limit >= 0 && limit < ct)
4600            ct = limit;
4601        Coord[] vl = new Coord[ct];
4602        double[] vec = new double[2];
4603        sobol.skipTo(rng.between(1000, 65000));
4604        EACH_SOBOL:
4605        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++)
4606        {
4607            sobol.fillVector(vec);
4608            xTarget = (int) (xTotal * vec[0]);
4609            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4610                if ((xTarget -= xCounts[x]) < 0) {
4611                    bestX = x;
4612                    yTotal = xCounts[x];
4613                    break;
4614                }
4615            }
4616            yTarget = (int) (yTotal * vec[1]);
4617
4618            for (int s = 0, y = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4619                t = data[bestX * ySections + s] | 0L;
4620                for (long cy = 1; cy != 0 && y < height; y++, cy <<= 1) {
4621                    if ((t & (cy|0L)) != 0 && --yTarget < 0) {
4622                        vl[i] = Coord.get(bestX, y);
4623                        continue EACH_SOBOL;
4624                    }
4625                }
4626            }
4627        }
4628        return vl;
4629
4630    }

4632    /**
4633     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a deterministic but random-seeming
4634     * scattering of chosen cells with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells
4635     * in this. This is pseudo-random with a fixed seed, but is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as
4636     * {@link #separatedRegionZCurve(double, int)}, and probably faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a
4637     * value for fraction), it will start to overlap, but a fraction value of 0.4 reliably has had no overlap in
4638     * testing. Does not restrict the size of the returned array other than only using up to
4639     * {@code fraction * size()} cells.
4640     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4641     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the quasi-random cells
4642     */
4643    public Coord[] mixedRandomSeparated(double fraction)
4644    {
4645        return mixedRandomSeparated(fraction, -1, 1L);
4646    }

4650     * scattering of chosen cells with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells
4651     * in this. This is pseudo-random with a fixed seed, but is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as
4652     * {@link #separatedRegionZCurve(double, int)}, and probably faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a
4653     * value for fraction), it will start to overlap, but a fraction value of 0.4 reliably has had no overlap in
4654     * testing. Restricts the total size of the returned array to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells
4655     * are "on"). If limit is negative, this will not restrict the size.
4656     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4657     * @param limit the maximum size of the array to return

4665    /**
4666     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a deterministic but random-seeming
4667     * scattering of chosen cells with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells
4668     * in this. This is pseudo-random with the given seed (which will be made into an odd number if it is not one
4669     * already), and is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as {@link #separatedZCurve(double, int)}, and
4670     * probably faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, but
4671     * a fraction value of 0.4 reliably has had no overlap in testing. Restricts the total size of the returned array to
4672     * a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells are "on"). If limit is negative, this will not restrict the
4673     * size.
4674     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4675     * @param limit the maximum size of the array to return
4676     * @param seed a long seed to change the points; the most significant 21 bits (except the sign bit) and least significant bit are ignored
4677     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the pseudo-random cells
4678     */
4679    public Coord[] mixedRandomSeparated(double fraction, int limit, long seed) {
4680        if (fraction < 0)
4681            return new Coord[0];
4682        if (fraction > 1)
4683            fraction = 1;
4684        int tmp, ic;
4685        long t, w;
4686        seed |= 1L;
4687        final int total = size();
4688        int ct = (int) (total * fraction);
4689        if (limit >= 0 && limit < ct)
4690            ct = limit;
4691        Coord[] vl = new Coord[ct];
4692        EACH_QUASI:
4693        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++) {
4694            tmp = (int) (VanDerCorputQRNG.altDetermine(seed, i + 1) * total);
4695
4696            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4697                for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4698                    if ((ic = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
4699                        t = data[x * ySections + s]|0L;
4700                        for (--ic; t != 0; ic--) {
4701                            w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
4702                            if (ic == tmp) {
4703                                vl[i] = Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.bitCount(w - 1));
4704                                continue EACH_QUASI;
4705                            }
4706                            t ^= w;
4707                        }
4708                    }
4709                }
4710            }
4711        }
4712        return vl;
4713    }

4720     * in this. This is pseudo-random with a fixed seed, and is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as
4721     * {@link #separatedRegionZCurve(double, int)}, and probably faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a

4731    /**
4732     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a deterministic but random-seeming subset of its previous contents,
4733     * choosing cells so that the {@link #size()} matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells
4734     * in this. This is pseudo-random with a fixed seed, and is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as
4735     * {@link #separatedRegionZCurve(double, int)}, and probably faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a
4736     * value for fraction), it will start to overlap, but a fraction value of 0.4 reliably has had no overlap in
4737     * testing. Restricts the total count of "on" cells after this returns to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0
4738     * if no cells are "on"). If limit is negative, this will not restrict the count.
4739     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4740     * @param limit the maximum count of "on" cells to keep

4743    public GreasedRegion mixedRandomRegion(double fraction, int limit) {

4746    /**
4747     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a deterministic but random-seeming subset of its previous contents,
4748     * choosing cells so that the {@link #size()} matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells
4749     * in this. This is pseudo-random with the given seed (which will be made into an odd number if it is not one
4750     * already), and is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as {@link #separatedZCurve(double, int)}, and
4751     * probably faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, but
4752     * a fraction value of 0.4 reliably has had no overlap in testing. Restricts the total count of "on" cells after
4753     * this returns to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells are "on"). If limit is negative, this will
4754     * not restrict the count.
4755     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4756     * @param limit the maximum count of "on" cells to keep
4757     * @return this for chaining
4758     */
4759    public GreasedRegion mixedRandomRegion(double fraction, int limit, long seed) {
4760        int idx, run = 0;
4761        final int total = size();
4762        if (total <= limit)
4763            return this;
4764        if (total <= 0)
4765            return empty();
4766        if (limit < 0)
4767            limit = (int) (fraction * ct);
4768        if(limit <= 0)
4769            return empty();
4770        seed |= 1L;
4771        int[] order = new int[limit];
4772        for (int i = 0, m = 1; i < limit; i++, m++) {
4773            idx = (int)(VanDerCorputQRNG.altDetermine(seed, m) * total);
4774            BIG:
4775            while (true) {
4776                for (int j = 0; j < i; j++) {
4777                    if (order[j] == idx) {
4778                        idx = (int)(VanDerCorputQRNG.altDetermine(seed, ++m) * total);
4779                        continue BIG;
4780                    }
4781                }
4782                break;
4783            }
4784            order[i] = idx;
4785        }
4786        idx = 0;
4787        Arrays.sort(order);
4788        long t, w;
4789        ALL:
4790        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4791            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4792                if ((t = data[x * ySections + s]|0L) != 0L) {
4793                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
4794                    while (w != 0) {
4795                        if (run++ == order[idx]) {
4796                            if (++idx >= limit) {
4797                                data[x * ySections + s] &= (w<<1)-1;
4798                                for (int rx = x+1; rx < width; rx++) {
4799                                    data[rx * ySections + s] = 0;
4800                                }
4801                                for (int rs = s+1; rs < ySections; rs++) {
4802                                    for (int rx = 0; rx < width; rx++) {
4803                                        data[rx * ySections + rs] = 0;
4804                                    }
4805                                }
4806                                break ALL;
4807                            }
4808                        } else {
4809                            data[x * ySections + s] ^= w;
4810                        }
4811                        t ^= w;
4812                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
4813                    }
4814                }
4815            }
4816        }
4817        tallied = false;
4818        return this;
4819    }

4821    /**
4822     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a quasi-random scattering of chosen cells
4823     * with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
4824     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
4825     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however.
4826     * Does not restrict the size of the returned array other than only using up to {@code fraction * size()} cells.
4827     * <br>
4828     * You can choose between {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double)}, {@link #separatedZCurve(double)}, and this method,
4829     * where all are quasi-random, mixedRandom is probably fastest, ZCurve may have better 2-dimensional gaps between
4830     * cells, and this method is somewhere in the middle.
4831     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4832     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the quasi-random cells
4833     */
4834    public Coord[] quasiRandomSeparated(double fraction)
4835    {
4836        return quasiRandomSeparated(fraction, -1);
4837    }

4839    /**
4840     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a quasi-random scattering of chosen cells
4841     * with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
4842     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
4843     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however.
4844     * Restricts the total size of the returned array to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells are "on").
4845     * If limit is negative, this will not restrict the size.
4846     * <br>
4847     * You can choose between {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double, int)}, {@link #separatedZCurve(double, int)}, and
4848     * this method, where all are quasi-random, mixedRandom is probably fastest, ZCurve may have better 2-dimensional
4849     * gaps between cells, and this method is somewhere in the middle.
4850     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4851     * @param limit the maximum size of the array to return
4852     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the quasi-random cells
4853     */
4854    public Coord[] quasiRandomSeparated(double fraction, int limit)
4855    {
4856        if(fraction < 0)
4857            return new Coord[0];
4858        if(fraction > 1)
4859            fraction = 1;
4860        int ct = 0, tmp, total, ic;
4861        long t, w;
4862        int[] counts = new int[width * ySections];
4863        for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
4864            tmp = Long.bitCount(data[i]);
4865            counts[i] = tmp == 0 ? -1 : (ct += tmp);
4866        }
4867        total = ct;
4868        ct *= fraction;// (int)(fraction * ct);
4869        if(limit >= 0 && limit < ct)
4870            ct = limit;
4871        Coord[] vl = new Coord[ct];
4872        EACH_QUASI:
4873        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++)
4874        {
4875            tmp = (int)(VanDerCorputQRNG.determine2(i ^ i >>> 1) * total);
4876            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4877                for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4878                    if ((ic = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
4879                        t = data[x * ySections + s];
4880                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
4881                        for (--ic; w != 0; ic--) {
4882                            if (ic == tmp) {
4883                                vl[i] = Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
4884                                continue EACH_QUASI;
4885                            }
4886                            t ^= w;
4887                            w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
4888                        }
4889                    }
4890                }
4891            }
4892            vl[i] = atFraction(tmp);
4893        }
4894        return vl;
4895    }

4900     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a quasi-random subset of its previous contents, choosing cells so that
4901     * the {@link #size()} matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
4902     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
4903     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however.
4904     * Does not restrict the count of "on" cells after this returns other than by only using up to
4905     * {@code fraction * size()} cells.
4906     * <br>
4907     * You can choose between {@link #mixedRandomRegion(double)}, {@link #separatedRegionZCurve(double)}, and this
4908     * method, where all are quasi-random, mixedRandom is probably fastest, ZCurve may have better 2-dimensional gaps
4909     * between cells, and this method is somewhere in the middle.
4910     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4911     * @return this for chaining

4916    /**
4917     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a quasi-random subset of its previous contents, choosing cells so that
4918     * the {@link #size()} matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
4919     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
4920     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however.
4921     * Restricts the total count of "on" cells after this returns to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no
4922     * cells are "on"). If limit is negative, this will not restrict the count.
4923     * <br>
4924     * You can choose between {@link #mixedRandomRegion(double, int)}, {@link #separatedRegionZCurve(double, int)}, and
4925     * this method, where all are quasi-random, mixedRandom is probably fastest, ZCurve may have better 2-dimensional
4926     * gaps between cells, and this method is somewhere in the middle.
4927     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4928     * @param limit the maximum count of "on" cells to keep
4929     * @return this for chaining
4930     */
4931    public GreasedRegion quasiRandomRegion(double fraction, int limit) {
4932        int ct = size(), idx, run = 0;
4933        if (ct <= limit)
4934            return this;
4935        if (ct <= 0)
4936            return empty();
4937        if (limit < 0)
4938            limit = (int) (fraction * ct);
4939        if(limit <= 0)
4940            return empty();
4941        int[] order = new int[limit];
4942        for (int i = 0, m = 1; i < limit; i++, m++) {
4943            idx = (int) (VanDerCorputQRNG.determine2(m) * ct);
4944            BIG:
4945            while (true) {
4946                for (int j = 0; j < i; j++) {
4947                    if (order[j] == idx) {
4948                        idx = (int) (VanDerCorputQRNG.determine2(++m) * ct);
4949                        continue BIG;
4950                    }
4951                }
4952                break;
4953            }
4954            order[i] = idx;
4955        }
4956        idx = 0;
4957        Arrays.sort(order);
4958        long t, w;
4959        ALL:
4960        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4961            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4962                if ((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0) {
4963                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
4964                    while (w != 0) {
4965                        if (run++ == order[idx]) {
4966                            if (++idx >= limit) {
4967                                data[x * ySections + s] &= (w<<1)-1;
4968                                for (int rx = x+1; rx < width; rx++) {
4969                                    data[rx * ySections + s] = 0;
4970                                }
4971                                for (int rs = s+1; rs < ySections; rs++) {
4972                                    for (int rx = 0; rx < width; rx++) {
4973                                        data[rx * ySections + rs] = 0;
4974                                    }
4975                                }
4976                                break ALL;
4977                            }
4978                        } else {
4979                            data[x * ySections + s] ^= w;
4980                        }
4981                        t ^= w;
4982                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
4983                    }
4984                }
4985            }
4986        }
4987        tallied = false;
4988        return this;
4989    }

4991    /**
4992     * Like {@link #retract()}, this removes the "on" cells that are 4-way-adjacent to any "off" cell, but unlike that
4993     * method it keeps a fraction of those surface cells, quasi-randomly selecting them. This can be thought of as
4994     * running {@link #surface()} on a copy of this GreasedRegion, running {@link #quasiRandomRegion(double)} on that
4995     * surface with the given fractionKept, taking the original GreasedRegion and removing its whole surface with
4996     * {@link #retract()}, then inserting the quasi-randomly-removed surface into this GreasedRegion to replace its
4997     * surface with a randomly "damaged" one.
4998     * @param fractionKept the fraction between 0.0 and 1.0 of how many cells on the outer surface of this to keep "on"
4999     * @return this for chaining
5000     */
5001    public GreasedRegion fray(double fractionKept)
5002    {
5003        GreasedRegion cpy = new GreasedRegion(this).retract();
5004        return xor(cpy).quasiRandomRegion(1.0 - fractionKept).or(cpy);
5005    }

5007    /**
5008     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a random subset of its previous contents, choosing cells so that the
5009     * distance between any two "on" cells is at least {@code minimumDistance}, with at least one cell as "on" if any
5010     * were "on" in this originally. Does not limit the count of "on" cells in the result.
5011     * @param rng used to generate random positions
5012     * @param minimumDistance the minimum distance between "on" cells in the result
5013     * @return this for chaining
5014     */
5015    public GreasedRegion randomScatter(IRNG rng, int minimumDistance) {
5016        return randomScatter(rng, minimumDistance, -1);
5017    }
5018    /**
5019     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a random subset of its previous contents, choosing cells so that the
5020     * distance between any two "on" cells is at least {@code minimumDistance}, with at least one cell as "on" if any
5021     * were "on" in this originally.
5022     * Restricts the total count of "on" cells after this returns to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no
5023     * cells are "on"). If limit is negative, this will not restrict the count.
5024     * @param rng used to generate random positions
5025     * @param minimumDistance the minimum distance between "on" cells in the result
5026     * @param limit the maximum count of "on" cells to keep
5027     * @return this for chaining
5028     */
5029    public GreasedRegion randomScatter(IRNG rng, int minimumDistance, int limit) {
5030        int tmp, total = 0, ct;
5031        tally();
5032        if(this.ct == 0)
5033            return this;
5034        if(limit == 0)
5035            return empty();
5036        else if(limit < 0)
5037            limit = width * height;
5038        long t, w;
5039        long[] data2 = new long[data.length];
5040        MAIN_LOOP:
5041        while (total < limit) { 
5042            if(!tallied) 
5043                tally();
5044            tmp = rng.nextInt(this.ct);
5045
5046            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5047                for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5048                    if ((ct = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
5049                        t = data[x * ySections + s];
5050                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5051                        for (--ct; w != 0; ct--) {
5052                            if (ct == tmp) {
5053                                removeRectangle(x - minimumDistance,
5054                                        ((s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)) - minimumDistance,
5055                                        minimumDistance << 1 | 1, minimumDistance << 1 | 1);
5056                                data2[x * ySections + s] |= w;
5057                                ++total;
5058                                continue MAIN_LOOP;
5059                            }
5060                            t ^= w;
5061                            w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5062                        }
5063                    }
5064                }
5065            }
5066            break;
5067        }
5068        data = data2;
5069        tallied = false;
5070        return this;
5071    }
5072
5073    public double rateDensity()
5074    {
5075        double sz = height * width;
5076        if(sz == 0)
5077            return 0;
5078        double onAmount = sz - size(), retractedOn = sz - copy().retract().size();
5079        return (onAmount + retractedOn) / (sz * 2.0);
5080    }
5081    public double rateRegularity()
5082    {
5083        GreasedRegion me2 = copy().surface8way();
5084        double irregularCount = me2.size();
5085        if(irregularCount == 0)
5086            return 0;
5087        return me2.remake(this).surface().size() / irregularCount;
5088    }
5089
5090    private static int median(int[] working, int start, int amount)
5091    {
5092        Arrays.sort(working, start, start + amount);
5093        if ((amount & 1) == 0) {
5094            return working[start + (amount >> 1) - 1] + working[start + (amount >> 1)] >>> 1;
5095        } else {
5096            return working[start + (amount >> 1)];
5097        }
5098    }
5099
5100    /**
5101     * Calculates a perceptual hash for this GreasedRegion using a method that is only precise for some sizes of
5102     * GreasedRegion; it writes a result to into, and uses working as a temporary buffer. The lengths of into and
5103     * working should be related; if into is length 1, then working should be length 64, and though the hash won't be
5104     * very detailed, it will work well for images with width and height that are multiples of 8; if into is length 4,
5105     * then working should be length 256, and this will work with more detail on images that have width and height that
5106     * are multiples of 16. If working is null or is too small, then this won't reuse it and will allocate an
5107     * appropriately-sized array for internal use.
5108     * <br>
5109     * Ported from https://github.com/commonsmachinery/blockhash/blob/master/blockhash.c , which is MIT-licensed.
5110     * @param into should be a long array of length 1 or 4; the contents don't matter and this will be where output is written to
5111     * @param working should be an int array of length 64 (if into has length 1) or 256 (if into has length 4); may be null if you like garbage collection
5112     */
5113    public void perceptualHashQuick(long[] into, int[] working)
5114    {
5115        final int bits = 8 << (Integer.numberOfTrailingZeros(Integer.highestOneBit(into.length)) >> 1);
5116        if(working == null || working.length < bits * bits)
5117            working = new int[bits * bits];
5118        final int blockWidth = width / bits, blockHeight = height / bits, blockWidthSections = blockWidth * ySections;
5119        if(blockHeight == 1)
5120        {
5121            for (int y = 0; y < bits; y++) {
5122                for (int x = 0; x < bits; x++) {
5123                    int value = 0;
5124                    for (int ix = 0; ix < blockWidthSections; ix += ySections) {
5125                        value += (data[x * blockWidthSections + ix + (y >> 6)] >>> (y & 63) & 1L);
5126                    }
5127                    working[x * bits + y] = value;
5128                }
5129            }
5130        }
5131        else if(blockHeight < 64 && Integer.bitCount(blockHeight) == 1) {
5132            final long yBlockMask = ~(-1L << blockHeight);
5133            final int divisorMask = (64 / blockHeight) - 1;
5134            long currentMask;
5135            int blockY = 0;
5136            for (int y = 0; y < bits; y++, blockY += blockHeight) {
5137                currentMask = yBlockMask << ((y & divisorMask) << blockHeight);
5138                for (int x = 0; x < bits; x++) {
5139                    int value = 0;
5140                    for (int ix = 0; ix < blockWidthSections; ix += ySections) {
5141                        value += Long.bitCount(data[x * blockWidthSections + ix + (blockY >> 6)] & currentMask);
5142                    }
5143                    working[x * bits + y] = value;
5144                }
5145            }
5146        }
5147        final int cellsPerBlock = blockWidth * blockHeight, numBlocks = bits * bits,
5148                halfCellCount = cellsPerBlock >>> 1;
5149        int bandSize = numBlocks >>> 2;
5150        int m, v;
5151        int currentInto = 0;
5152        long currentIntoPos = 1L;
5153        for (int i = 0; i < 4; i++) {
5154            m = median(working, i * bandSize, bandSize);
5155            for (int j = i * bandSize; j < (i + 1) * bandSize; j++) {
5156                v = working[j];
5157                if(v > m || (v - m == 0 && m > halfCellCount)) into[currentInto] |= currentIntoPos;
5158                if((currentIntoPos <<= 1) == 0)
5159                {
5160                    ++currentInto;
5161                    currentIntoPos = 1L;
5162                }
5163            }
5164        }
5165    }

5167    /*
5168    // This showed a strong x-y correlation because it didn't have a way to use a non-base-2 van der Corput sequence.
5169    // It also produced very close-together points, unfortunately.
5170    public static double quasiRandomX(int idx)
5171    {
5172        return atVDCSequence(26 + idx * 5);
5173    }
5174    public static double quasiRandomY(int idx)
5175    {
5176        return atVDCSequence(19 + idx * 3);
5177    }
5178
5179    private static double atVDCSequence(int idx)
5180    {
5181        int leading = Integer.numberOfLeadingZeros(idx);
5182        return (Integer.reverse(idx) >>> leading) / (1.0 * (1 << (32 - leading)));
5183    }
5184    */
5185    public Coord[] asCoords()
5186    {
5187        return asCoords(new Coord[size()]);
5188
5189    }
5190    public Coord[] asCoords(Coord[] points)
5191    {
5192        if(points == null)
5193            points = new Coord[size()];
5194        int idx = 0, len = points.length;
5195        long t, w;
5196        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5197            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5198                if((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0)
5199                {
5200                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5201                    while (w != 0) {
5202                        if(idx >= len) return points;
5203                        points[idx++] = Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5204                        t ^= w;
5205                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5206                    }
5207                }
5208            }
5209        }
5210        return points;
5211    }
5212    public int[] asEncoded()
5213    {
5214        int ct = size(), idx = 0;
5215        int[] points = new int[ct];
5216        long t, w;
5217        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5218            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5219                if((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0)
5220                {
5221                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5222                    while (w != 0) {
5223                        points[idx++] = Coord.pureEncode(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5224                        t ^= w;
5225                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5226                    }
5227                }
5228            }
5229        }
5230        return points;
5231    }
5232    public int[] asTightEncoded()
5233    {
5234        int ct = size(), idx = 0;
5235        int[] points = new int[ct];
5236        long t, w;
5237        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5238            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5239                if((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0)
5240                {
5241                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5242                    while (w != 0) {
5243                        points[idx++] =  ((s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)) * width + x;
5244                        t ^= w;
5245                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5246                    }
5247                }
5248            }
5249        }
5250        return points;
5251    }

5253    /**
5254     * @return All cells in this zone.
5255     */
5256    @Override
5257    public List<Coord> getAll() {
5258        ArrayList<Coord> points = new ArrayList<>();
5259        long t, w;
5260        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5261            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5262                if((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0)
5263                {
5264                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5265                    while (w != 0) {
5266                        points.add(Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)));
5267                        t ^= w;
5268                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5269                    }
5270                }
5271            }
5272        }
5273        return points;
5274
5275    }

5277    public Coord first()
5278    {
5279        long w;
5280        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5281            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5282                if ((w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(data[x * ySections + s])) != 0) {
5283                    return Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5284                }
5285            }
5286        }
5287        return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5288    }
5289
5290    public int firstTight()
5291    {
5292        long w;
5293        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5294            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5295                if ((w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(data[x * ySections + s])) != 0) {
5296                    return ((s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)) * width + x;
5297                }
5298            }
5299        }
5300        return -1;
5301    }
5302    public Coord nth(final int index)
5303    {
5304        if(index < 0)
5305            return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5306        int ct = size(), tmp;
5307        if(index >= ct)
5308            return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5309        long t, w;
5310        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5311            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5312                if ((ct = counts[x * ySections + s]) > index) {
5313                    t = data[x * ySections + s];
5314                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5315                    for (--ct; w != 0; ct--) {
5316                        if (ct == index)
5317                            return Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5318                        t ^= w;
5319                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5320                    }
5321                }
5322            }
5323        }
5324        return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5325    }
5326
5327    public Coord atFraction(final double fraction)
5328    {
5329        int ct = size(), tmp;
5330        if(ct <= 0) return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5331        tmp = Math.abs((int)(fraction * ct) % ct);
5332        long t, w;
5333        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5334            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5335                if ((ct = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
5336                    t = data[x * ySections + s];
5337                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5338                    for (--ct; w != 0; ct--) {
5339                        if (ct == tmp)
5340                            return Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5341                        t ^= w;
5342                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5343                    }
5344                }
5345            }
5346        }
5347        return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5348    }
5349
5350    public int atFractionTight(final double fraction)
5351    {
5352        int ct = size(), tmp;
5353        if(ct <= 0) return -1;
5354        tmp = Math.abs((int)(fraction * ct) % ct);
5355        long t, w;
5356
5357        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5358            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5359                if ((ct = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
5360                    t = data[x * ySections + s];
5361                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5362                    for (--ct; w != 0; ct--) {
5363                        if (ct == tmp)
5364                            return ((s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)) * width + x;
5365                        t ^= w;
5366                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5367                    }
5368                }
5369            }
5370        }
5371        return -1;
5372    }
5373
5374    /**
5375     * Gets a single random Coord from the "on" positions in this GreasedRegion, or the Coord (-1,-1) if this is empty.
5376     * Uses the given IRNG to generate one random int, which is used as an index. The technique this uses to iterate
5377     * over bits can be credited to Erling Ellingsen and Daniel Lemire, found
5378     * <a href="https://lemire.me/blog/2013/12/23/even-faster-bitmap-decoding/">here</a>, and seems to be a little
5379     * faster than the previous method. The fastest way to get a random Coord from a GreasedRegion is to avoid iterating
5380     * over the bits at all, so if your region data doesn't change you should get it as a Coord array with
5381     * {@link #asCoords()} and call {@link IRNG#getRandomElement(Object[])} with that array as the parameter. If you
5382     * take the asCoords() call out of consideration, getting random elements out of an array (especially a large one)
5383     * can be hundreds of times faster.
5384     * @param rng an IRNG such as an {@link RNG} or {@link GWTRNG}
5385     * @return a single randomly-chosen Coord from the "on" positions in this GreasedRegion, or (-1,-1) if empty
5386     */
5387    public Coord singleRandom(IRNG rng)
5388    {
5389        int ct = size(), tmp = rng.nextInt(ct);
5390        long t, w;
5391        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5392            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5393                if ((ct = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
5394                    t = data[x * ySections + s] | 0L;
5395                    for (--ct; t != 0; ct--) {
5396                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5397                        if (ct == tmp)
5398                            return Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.bitCount(w-1));
5399                        t ^= w;
5400                    }
5401                }
5402            }
5403        }
5404        return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5405    }
5406
5407    public int singleRandomTight(IRNG rng)
5408    {
5409        int ct = size(), tmp = rng.nextInt(ct);
5410        long t, w;
5411        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5412            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5413                if ((ct = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
5414                    t = data[x * ySections + s];
5415                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5416                    for (--ct; w != 0; ct--) {
5417                        if (ct == tmp)
5418                            return ((s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)) * width + x;
5419                        t ^= w;
5420                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5421                    }
5422                }
5423            }
5424        }
5425
5426        return -1;
5427    }
