5429    /**
5430     * Narrow-purpose; takes an x and a y value, each between 0 and 65535 inclusive, and interleaves their bits so the
5431     * least significant bit and every other bit after it are filled with the bits of x, while the
5432     * second-least-significant bit and every other bit after that are filled with the bits of y. Essentially, this
5433     * takes two numbers with bits labeled like {@code a b c} for x and {@code R S T} for y and makes a number with
5434     * those bits arranged like {@code R a S b T c}.
5435     * @param x an int between 0 and 65535, inclusive
5436     * @param y an int between 0 and 65535, inclusive
5437     * @return an int that interleaves x and y, with x in the least significant bit position
5438     */
5439    public static int interleaveBits(int x, int y)
5440    {
5441        x |= y << 16;
5442        x =    ((x & 0x0000ff00) << 8) | ((x >>> 8) & 0x0000ff00) | (x & 0xff0000ff);
5443        x =    ((x & 0x00f000f0) << 4) | ((x >>> 4) & 0x00f000f0) | (x & 0xf00ff00f);
5444        x =    ((x & 0x0c0c0c0c) << 2) | ((x >>> 2) & 0x0c0c0c0c) | (x & 0xc3c3c3c3);
5445        return ((x & 0x22222222) << 1) | ((x >>> 1) & 0x22222222) | (x & 0x99999999);
5446    }
5447
5448    /**
5449     * Narrow-purpose; takes an int that represents a distance down the Z-order curve and moves its bits around so that
5450     * its x component is stored in the bottom 16 bits (use {@code (n & 0xffff)} to obtain) and its y component is
5451     * stored in the upper 16 bits (use {@code (n >>> 16)} to obtain). This may be useful for ordering traversals of all
5452     * points in a GreasedRegion less predictably.
5453     * @param n an int that has already been interleaved, though this can really be any int
5454     * @return an int with x in its lower bits ({@code x = n & 0xffff;}) and y in its upper bits ({@code y = n >>> 16;})
5455     */
5456    public static int disperseBits(int n)
5457    {
5458        n =    ((n & 0x22222222) << 1) | ((n >>> 1) & 0x22222222) | (n & 0x99999999);
5459        n =    ((n & 0x0c0c0c0c) << 2) | ((n >>> 2) & 0x0c0c0c0c) | (n & 0xc3c3c3c3);
5460        n =    ((n & 0x00f000f0) << 4) | ((n >>> 4) & 0x00f000f0) | (n & 0xf00ff00f);
5461        return ((n & 0x0000ff00) << 8) | ((n >>> 8) & 0x0000ff00) | (n & 0xff0000ff);
5462    }
5463    private static int nextPowerOfTwo(int n)
5464    {
5465        final int highest = Integer.highestOneBit(n);
5466        return  (highest == NumberTools.lowestOneBit(n)) ? highest : highest << 1;
5467    }
5468
5469    /**
5470     * Like {@link #nth(int)}, this gets the Coord at a given index along a path through the GreasedRegion, but unlike
5471     * nth(), this traverses the path in a zig-zag pattern called the Z-Order Curve. This method is often not very fast
5472     * compared to nth(), but this different path can help if iteration needs to seem less regular while still covering
5473     * all "on" cells in the GresedRegion eventually.
5474     * @param index the distance along the Z-order curve to travel, only counting "on" cells in this GreasedRegion.
5475     * @return the Coord at the given distance, or the Coord with x and y both -1 if index is too high or low
5476     */
5477    public Coord nthZCurve(final int index)
5478    {
5479        int ct = -1, x, y, s, d, max = nextPowerOfTwo(width) * nextPowerOfTwo(height);
5480        long t, w;
5481        for (int o = 0; o < max; o++) {
5482            d = disperseBits(o);
5483            x = d & 0xffff;
5484            y = d >>> 16;
5485            if(x >= width && y >= height)
5486                break;
5487            if(x >= width)
5488                continue;
5489            if(y >= height)
5490                continue;
5491            s = d >>> 22;
5492            t = data[x * ySections + s];
5493            if((ct += (t >>> (y & 63) & 1L)) == index)
5494                return Coord.get(x, y);
5495        }
5496        return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5497    }
5498    /**
5499     * Like {@link #nth(int)}, this finds a given index along a path through the GreasedRegion, but unlike nth(), this
5500     * traverses the path in a zig-zag pattern called the Z-Order Curve, and unlike {@link #nthZCurve(int)}, this does
5501     * not return a Coord and instead produces a "tight"-encoded int. This method is often not very fast compared to
5502     * nth(), but this different path can help if iteration needs to seem less regular while still covering all "on"
5503     * cells in the GreasedRegion eventually, and the tight encoding may be handy if you need to use ints.
5504     * @param index the distance along the Z-order curve to travel, only counting "on" cells in this GreasedRegion.
5505     * @return the "tight" encoded point at the given distance, or -1 if index is too high or low
5506     */
5507
5508    public int nthZCurveTight(final int index)
5509    {
5510        int ct = -1, x, y, s, d, max = nextPowerOfTwo(width) * nextPowerOfTwo(height);
5511        long t;
5512        for (int o = 0; o < max; o++) {
5513            d = disperseBits(o);
5514            x = d & 0xffff;
5515            y = d >>> 16;
5516            if(x >= width && y >= height)
5517                break;
5518            if(x >= width)
5519                continue;
5520            if(y >= height)
5521                continue;
5522            s = d >>> 22;
5523            t = data[x * ySections + s];
5524            if((ct += (t >>> (y & 63) & 1L)) == index)
5525                return y * width + x;
5526        }
5527        return -1;
5528    }
5529
5530    /**
5531     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a quasi-random scattering of chosen cells
5532     * with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
5533     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
5534     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however. Contrast with
5535     * {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double, int)}, which tends to overlap more frequently. This method seems to work
5536     * well because it chooses quasi-random points by their index in the Z-Order Curve as opposed to the simpler
5537     * approach mixedRandomSeparated uses to traverse points (which just runs through the "on" cells a column at a time,
5538     * not caring if two points are in adjacent cells as long as they are in different columns). Testing with a dungeon
5539     * layout of mostly-on cells, this method has no overlap with a fraction of 0.4, while mixedRandomSeparated has
5540     * overlap as early as 0.15 for fraction, and it only gets worse at higher values. A change to the algorithm used by
5541     * {@link #quasiRandomSeparated(double)} has it overlapping at the same rate as this method, though it should be
5542     * much faster. This method can be especially slow, since each Z-Order traversal may need to try many cells that are
5543     * outside the GreasedRegion but are on the Z-Order Curve.
5544     * Does not restrict the size of the returned array other than only using up to {@code fraction * size()} cells.
5545     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
5546     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the quasi-random cells
5547     */
5548    public Coord[] separatedZCurve(double fraction)
5549    {
5550        return separatedZCurve(fraction, -1);
5551    }
5552
5553    /**
5554     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a quasi-random scattering of chosen cells
5555     * with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
5556     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
5557     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however. Contrast with
5558     * {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double, int)}, which tends to overlap more frequently. This method seems to work
5559     * well because it chooses quasi-random points by their index in the Z-Order Curve as opposed to the simpler
5560     * approach mixedRandomSeparated uses to traverse points (which just runs through the "on" cells a column at a time,
5561     * not caring if two points are in adjacent cells as long as they are in different columns). Testing with a dungeon
5562     * layout of mostly-on cells, this method has no overlap with a fraction of 0.4, while mixedRandomSeparated has
5563     * overlap as early as 0.15 for fraction, and it only gets worse at higher values. A change to the algorithm used by
5564     * {@link #quasiRandomSeparated(double, int)} has it overlapping at the same rate as this method, though it should
5565     * be much faster. This method can be especially slow, since each Z-Order traversal may need to try many cells that
5566     * are outside the GreasedRegion but are on the Z-Order Curve.
5567     * Restricts the total size of the returned array to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells are "on").
5568     * If limit is negative, this will not restrict the size.
5569     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
5570     * @param limit the maximum size of the array to return
5571     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the quasi-random cells
5572     */
5573    public Coord[] separatedZCurve(double fraction, int limit)
5574    {
5575        if(fraction < 0)
5576            return new Coord[0];
5577        if(fraction > 1)
5578            fraction = 1;
5579        int ct = size(), total;
5580        total = ct;
5581        ct *= fraction;
5582        if(limit >= 0 && limit < ct)
5583            ct = limit;
5584        Coord[] vl = new Coord[ct];
5585        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++)
5586        {
5587            vl[i] = nthZCurve((int) (VanDerCorputQRNG.determine2(i ^ i >>> 1) * total));
5588        }
5589        return vl;
5590    }
5591    /**
5592     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a quasi-random subset of its previous contents, choosing cells so that
5593     * the {@link #size()} matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
5594     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
5595     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however. Contrast with
5596     * {@link #mixedRandomRegion(double)}, which tends to overlap more frequently. This method seems to work
5597     * well because it chooses quasi-random points by their index in the Z-Order Curve as opposed to the simpler
5598     * approach mixedRandomRegion uses to traverse points (which just runs through the "on" cells a column at a time,
5599     * not caring if two points are in adjacent cells as long as they are in different columns). Testing with a dungeon
5600     * layout of mostly-on cells, this method has no overlap with a fraction of 0.4, while mixedRandomRegion has
5601     * overlap as early as 0.15 for fraction, and it only gets worse at higher values. A change to the algorithm used by
5602     * {@link #quasiRandomRegion(double)} has it overlapping at the same rate as this method, though it should be much
5603     * faster. This method can be especially slow, since each Z-Order traversal may need to try many cells that are
5604     * outside the GreasedRegion but are on the Z-Order Curve.
5605     * Does not restrict the size of the returned array other than only using up to {@code fraction * size()} cells.
5606     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
5607     * @return this, after modifications, for chaining
5608     */
5609    public GreasedRegion separatedRegionZCurve(double fraction)
5610    {
5611        return separatedRegionZCurve(fraction, -1);
5612    }
5613
5614    /**
5615     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a quasi-random subset of its previous contents, choosing cells so that
5616     * the {@link #size()} matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
5617     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
5618     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however. Contrast with
5619     * {@link #mixedRandomRegion(double, int)}, which tends to overlap more frequently. This method seems to work
5620     * well because it chooses quasi-random points by their index in the Z-Order Curve as opposed to the simpler
5621     * approach mixedRandomRegion uses to traverse points (which just runs through the "on" cells a column at a time,
5622     * not caring if two points are in adjacent cells as long as they are in different columns). Testing with a dungeon
5623     * layout of mostly-on cells, this method has no overlap with a fraction of 0.4, while mixedRandomRegion has
5624     * overlap as early as 0.15 for fraction, and it only gets worse at higher values. A change to the algorithm used by
5625     * {@link #quasiRandomRegion(double, int)} has it overlapping at the same rate as this method, though it should be
5626     * much faster. This method can be especially slow, since each Z-Order traversal may need to try many cells that
5627     * are outside the GreasedRegion but are on the Z-Order Curve.
5628     * Restricts the total size of the returned array to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells are "on").
5629     * If limit is negative, this will not restrict the size.
5630     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
5631     * @param limit the maximum size of the array to return
5632     * @return this, after modifications, for chaining
5633     */
5634    public GreasedRegion separatedRegionZCurve(double fraction, int limit)
5635    {
5636        if(fraction <= 0)
5637            return empty();
5638        if(fraction >= 1)
5639            return this;
5640        int ct = size(), total;
5641        if(limit >= ct)
5642            return this;
5643        total = ct;
5644        ct *= fraction;
5645        if(limit >= 0 && limit < ct)
5646            ct = limit;
5647        int[] vl = new int[ct];
5648        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++)
5649        {
5650            vl[i] = nthZCurveTight((int) (VanDerCorputQRNG.determine2(i ^ i >>> 1) * total));
5651        }
5652        return empty().insertSeveral(vl);
5653    }
5654
5655
5656    public Coord[] randomPortion(IRNG rng, int size)
5657    {
5658        int ct = size(), idx = 0, run = 0;
5659        if(ct <= 0 || size <= 0)
5660            return new Coord[0];
5661        if(ct <= size)
5662            return asCoords();
5663        Coord[] points = new Coord[size];
5664        int[] order = rng.randomOrdering(ct);
5665        Arrays.sort(order, 0, size);
5666        long t, w;
5667        ALL:
5668        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5669            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5670                if((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0)
5671                {
5672                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5673                    while (w != 0) {
5674                        if (run++ == order[idx]) {
5675                            points[idx++] = Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5676                            if (idx >= size) break ALL;
5677                        }
5678                        t ^= w;
5679                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5680                    }
5681                }
5682            }
5683        }
5684        return points;
5685    }
5686
5687    public GreasedRegion randomRegion(IRNG rng, int size)
5688    {
5689        int ct = size(), idx = 0, run = 0;
5690        if(ct <= 0 || size <= 0)
5691            return empty();
5692        if(ct <= size)
5693            return this;
5694        int[] order = rng.randomOrdering(ct);
5695        Arrays.sort(order, 0, size);
5696        long t, w;
5697        ALL:
5698        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5699            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5700                if((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0)
5701                {
5702                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5703                    while (w != 0) {
5704                        if (run++ == order[idx]) {
5705                            if(++idx >= size) break ALL;
5706                        }
5707                        else
5708                        {
5709                            data[x * ySections + s] &= ~(1L << Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5710                        }
5711                        t ^= w;
5712                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5713                    }
5714                }
5715            }
5716        }
5717        tallied = false;
5718        return this;
5719    }
5720
5721    @Override
5722    public boolean contains(int x, int y)
5723    {
5724        return x >= 0 && y >= 0 && x < width && y < height && ySections > 0 &&
5725                ((data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0);
5726    }

5729    /**
5730     * @return Whether this zone is empty.
5731     */
5732    @Override
5733    public boolean isEmpty() {
5734        if(tallied) return ct > 0;
5735        for (int i = 0; i < data.length; i++) {
5736            if(data[i] != 0L) return false;
5737        }
5738        return true;
5739    }

5741    /**
5742     * Generates a 2D int array from an array or vararg of GreasedRegions, starting at all 0 and adding 1 to the int at
5743     * a position once for every GreasedRegion that has that cell as "on." This means if you give 8 GreasedRegions to
5744     * this method, it can produce any number between 0 and 8 in a cell; if you give 16 GreasedRegions, then it can
5745     * produce any number between 0 and 16 in a cell.
5746     * @param regions an array or vararg of GreasedRegions; must all have the same width and height
5747     * @return a 2D int array with the same width and height as the regions, where an int cell equals the number of given GreasedRegions that had an "on" cell at that position
5748     */
5749    public static int[][] sum(GreasedRegion... regions)
5750    {
5751        if(regions == null || regions.length <= 0)
5752            return new int[0][0];
5753        int w = regions[0].width, h = regions[0].height, l = regions.length, ys = regions[0].ySections;
5754        int[][] numbers = new int[w][h];
5755        for (int x = 0; x < w; x++) {
5756            for (int y = 0; y < h; y++) {
5757                for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
5758                    numbers[x][y] += (regions[i].data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? 1 : 0;
5759                }
5760            }
5761        }
5762        return numbers;
5763    }

5768     * this method, it can produce any number between 0 and 8 in a cell; if you give 16 GreasedRegions, then it can

5772     */

5776            return new int[0][0];

5779        int[][] numbers = new int[w][h];
5780        for (int x = 0; x < w; x++) {
5781            for (int y = 0; y < h; y++) {
5782                for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
5783                    numbers[x][y] += (regions.get(i).data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? 1 : 0;
5784                }
5785            }
5786        }
5787        return numbers;
5788    }

5839    /**
5840     * Generates a 2D int array from an array of GreasedRegions and an array of weights, starting the 2D result at all 0
5841     * and, for every GreasedRegion that has that cell as "on," adding the int in the corresponding weights array at
5842     * the position of that cell. This means if you give an array of 4 GreasedRegions to this method along with the
5843     * weights {@code 1, 2, 3, 4}, it can produce a number between 0 and 10 in a cell (where 10 is used when all 4
5844     * GreasedRegions have a cell "on," since {@code 1 + 2 + 3 + 4 == 10}); if the weights are instead
5845     * {@code 1, 10, 100, 1000}, then the results can vary between 0 and 1111, where 1111 is only if all GreasedRegions
5846     * have a cell as "on." The weights array must have a length at least equal to the length of the regions array.
5847     * @param regions an array of GreasedRegions; must all have the same width and height
5848     * @param weights an array of ints; must have length at least equal to regions' length
5849     * @return a 2D int array with the same width and height as the regions, where an int cell equals the sum of the weights corresponding to GreasedRegions that had an "on" cell at that position
5850     */
5851    public static int[][] sumWeighted(GreasedRegion[] regions, int[] weights)
5852    {
5853        if(regions == null || regions.length <= 0 || weights == null || weights.length < regions.length)
5854            return new int[0][0];
5855        int w = regions[0].width, h = regions[0].height, l = regions.length, ys = regions[0].ySections;
5856        int[][] numbers = new int[w][h];
5857        for (int x = 0; x < w; x++) {
5858            for (int y = 0; y < h; y++) {
5859                for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
5860                    numbers[x][y] += (regions[i].data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? weights[i] : 0;
5861                }
5862            }
5863        }
5864        return numbers;
5865    }

5878     */
5879    public static double[][] sumWeightedDouble(GreasedRegion[] regions, double[] weights)

5889                }
5890            }

5895    /**
5896     * Adds to an existing 2D int array with an array or vararg of GreasedRegions, adding 1 to the int in existing at
5897     * a position once for every GreasedRegion that has that cell as "on." This means if you give 8 GreasedRegions to
5898     * this method, it can increment by any number between 0 and 8 in a cell; if you give 16 GreasedRegions, then it can
5899     * increase the value in existing by any number between 0 and 16 in a cell.
5900     * @param existing a non-null 2D int array that will have each cell incremented by the sum of the GreasedRegions
5901     * @param regions an array or vararg of GreasedRegions; must all have the same width and height
5902     * @return existing, after modification, where an int cell will be changed by the number of given GreasedRegions that had an "on" cell at that position
5903     */
5904    public static int[][] sumInto(int[][] existing, GreasedRegion... regions)
5905    {
5906        if(regions == null || regions.length <= 0 || existing == null || existing.length == 0 || existing[0].length == 0)
5907            return existing;
5908        int w = existing.length, h = existing[0].length, l = regions.length, ys;
5909        for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
5910            GreasedRegion region = regions[i];
5911            ys = region.ySections;
5912            for (int x = 0; x < w && x < region.width; x++) {
5913                for (int y = 0; y < h && y < region.height; y++) {
5914                    existing[x][y] += (region.data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? 1 : 0;
5915                }
5916            }
5917        }
5918        return existing;
5919    }

5925     * this method, it can increment by any number between 0 and 8 in a cell; if you give 16 GreasedRegions, then it can

5930     */
5931    public static double[][] sumIntoDouble(double[][] existing, GreasedRegion... regions)

5934            return existing;

5936        for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {

5938                for (int y = 0; y < h && y < regions[i].height; y++) {
5939                    existing[x][y] += (regions[i].data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? 1.0 : 0.0;
5940                }
5941            }
5942        }
5943        return existing;

5946    /**
5947     * Discouraged from active use; slower than {@link squidpony.squidai.DijkstraMap} and has less features.
5948     * @param map a 2D char array where '#' is a wall
5949     * @param goals an array or vararg of Coord to get the distances toward
5950     * @return a 2D double array of distances from a cell to the nearest goal
5951     */
5952    public static double[][] dijkstraScan(char[][] map, Coord... goals)
5953    {
5954        if(map == null || map.length <= 0 || map[0].length <= 0 || goals == null || goals.length <= 0)
5955            return new double[0][0];
5956        int w = map.length, h = map[0].length, ys = (h + 63) >>> 6;
5957        double[][] numbers = new double[w][h];
5958        GreasedRegion walls = new GreasedRegion(map, '#'), floors = new GreasedRegion(walls).not(),
5959                middle = new GreasedRegion(w, h, goals).and(floors);
5960        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> regions = middle.floodSeriesToLimit(floors);
5961        int l = regions.size();
5962        for (int x = 0; x < w; x++) {
5963            for (int y = 0; y < h; y++) {
5964                for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
5965                    numbers[x][y] += (regions.get(i).data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? 1 : 0;
5966                }
5967            }
5968        }
5969        return numbers;
5970    }

5972     * Discouraged from active use; slower than {@link squidpony.squidai.DijkstraMap} and has less features.
5973     * @param map a 2D char array where '#' is a wall

5984                middle = new GreasedRegion(w, h, goals).and(floors);
5985        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> regions = middle.floodSeriesToLimit8way(floors);
5986        int l = regions.size();

5997    /**
5998     * Generates a 2D int array from an array or vararg of GreasedRegions, treating each cell in the nth region as the
5999     * nth bit of the int at the corresponding x,y cell in the int array. This means if you give 8 GreasedRegions to
6000     * this method, it can produce any 8-bit number in a cell (0-255); if you give 16 GreasedRegions, then it can
6001     * produce any 16-bit number (0-65535).
6002     * @param regions an array or vararg of GreasedRegions; must all have the same width and height
6003     * @return a 2D int array with the same width and height as the regions, with bits per int taken from the regions
6004     */
6005    public static int[][] bitSum(GreasedRegion... regions)
6006    {
6007        if(regions == null || regions.length <= 0)
6008            return new int[0][0];
6009        int w = regions[0].width, h = regions[0].height, l = Math.min(32, regions.length), ys = regions[0].ySections;
6010        int[][] numbers = new int[w][h];
6011        for (int x = 0; x < w; x++) {
6012            for (int y = 0; y < h; y++) {
6013                for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
6014                    numbers[x][y] |= (regions[i].data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? 1 << i : 0;
6015                }
6016            }
6017        }
6018        return numbers;
6019    }

6036    @Override
6037    public boolean equals(Object o) {
6038        if (this == o) return true;
6039        if (o == null || getClass() != o.getClass()) return false;
6040
6041        GreasedRegion that = (GreasedRegion) o;
6042
6043        if (height != that.height) return false;
6044        if (width != that.width) return false;
6045        if (ySections != that.ySections) return false;
6046        if (yEndMask != that.yEndMask) return false;
6047        return Arrays.equals(data, that.data);
6048    }

6050    @Override
6051    public int hashCode() {
6052        long result = 0x1A976FDF6BF60B8EL, z = 0x60642E2A34326F15L;
6053        final int len = data.length;
6054        for (int i = 0; i < len; i++) {
6055            result ^= (z += (data[i] ^ 0xC6BC279692B5CC85L) * 0x6C8E9CF570932BABL);
6056            result = (result << 54 | result >>> 10);
6057        }
6058        result ^= (z += (height ^ 0xC6BC279692B5CC85L) * 0x6C8E9CF570932BABL);
6059        result = (result << 54 | result >>> 10);
6060        result ^= (z += (width ^ 0xC6BC279692B5CC85L) * 0x6C8E9CF570932BABL);
6061        result = (result << 54 | result >>> 10);
6062
6063        result += (z ^ z >>> 26) * 0x632BE59BD9B4E019L;
6064        result = (result ^ result >>> 33) * 0xFF51AFD7ED558CCDL;
6065        return (int)((result ^ result >>> 33) * 0xC4CEB9FE1A85EC53L);
6066    }
6067    public long hash64() {
6068        long result = 0x1A976FDF6BF60B8EL, z = 0x60642E2A34326F15L;
6069        final int len = data.length;
6070        for (int i = 0; i < len; i++) {
6071            result ^= (z += (data[i] ^ 0xC6BC279692B5CC85L) * 0x6C8E9CF570932BABL);
6072            result = (result << 54 | result >>> 10);
6073        }
6074        result ^= (z += (height ^ 0xC6BC279692B5CC85L) * 0x6C8E9CF570932BABL);
6075        result = (result << 54 | result >>> 10);
6076        result ^= (z += (width ^ 0xC6BC279692B5CC85L) * 0x6C8E9CF570932BABL);
6077        result = (result << 54 | result >>> 10);
6078        
6079        result += (z ^ z >>> 26) * 0x632BE59BD9B4E019L;
6080        result = (result ^ result >>> 33) * 0xFF51AFD7ED558CCDL;
6081        return ((result ^ result >>> 33) * 0xC4CEB9FE1A85EC53L);
6082    }
6083
6084    public String serializeToString()
6085    {
6086        return width +
6087                "," + height +
6088                "," + StringKit.joinAlt(",",data);
6089    }
6090    public static GreasedRegion deserializeFromString(String s)
6091    {
6092        if(s == null || s.isEmpty())
6093            return null;
6094        int gap = s.indexOf(','), w = Integer.parseInt(s.substring(0, gap)),
6095                gap2 = s.indexOf(',', gap+1), h = Integer.parseInt(s.substring(gap+1, gap2));
6096        String[] splits = StringKit.split(s.substring(gap2+1), ",");
6097        long[] data = new long[splits.length];
6098        for (int i = 0; i < splits.length; i++) {
6099            data[i] = StringKit.longFromDec(splits[i]);
6100        }
6101        return new GreasedRegion(data, w, h);
6102    }

6104    /**
6105     * Constructs a GreasedRegion using a vararg for data. Primarily meant for generated code, since
6106     * {@link #serializeToString()} produces a String that happens to be a valid parameter list for this method.
6107     * @param width width of the GreasedRegion to produce
6108     * @param height height of the GreasedRegion to produce
6109     * @param data array or vararg of long containing the exact data, probably from an existing GreasedRegion
6110     * @return a new GreasedRegion with the given width, height, and data
6111     */
6112    public static GreasedRegion of(final int width, final int height, final long... data)
6113    {
6114        return new GreasedRegion(data, width, height);
6115    }
6116
6117    public String toCompressedString()
6118    {
6119        if(height > 0x4000)
6120            throw new UnsupportedOperationException("Height is too large to compress, aborting.");
6121        StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(width * height >> 2);
6122        boolean on = false;
6123        int span = 0;
6124        char adjust = (char) nextPowerOfTwo(Math.max(height, 32));
6125        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6126            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
6127                if(((data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) == 0) == on)
6128                    span++;
6129                else
6130                {
6131                    on = !on;
6132                    sb.append((char)(adjust | span));
6133                    span = 1;
6134                }
6135            }
6136            if(on)
6137            {
6138                sb.append((char)(adjust | span));
6139            }
6140            sb.append('\n');
6141            on = false;
6142            span = 0;
6143        }
6144        return sb.toString();
6145    }

6229    @Override
6230    public boolean retainAll(Collection<?> c) {
6231        GreasedRegion g2 = new GreasedRegion(width, height);
6232        for(Object o : c)
6233        {
6234            if(contains(o) && o instanceof Coord)
6235            {
6236                g2.add((Coord)o);
6237            }
6238        }
6239        boolean changed = equals(g2);
6240        remake(g2);
6241        return changed;
6242    }

6244    /**
6245     * Randomly removes points from a GreasedRegion, with larger values for preservation keeping more of the existing
6246     * shape intact. If preservation is 1, roughly 1/2 of all points will be removed; if 2, roughly 1/4, if 3, roughly
6247     * 1/8, and so on, so that preservation can be thought of as a negative exponent of 2.
6248     * @param rng used to determine random factors
6249     * @param preservation roughly what degree of points to remove (higher keeps more); removes about {@code 1/(2^preservation)} points
6250     * @return a randomly modified change to this GreasedRegion
6251     */
6252    public GreasedRegion deteriorate(RandomnessSource rng, int preservation) {
6253        if(rng == null || width <= 2 || ySections <= 0 || preservation <= 0)
6254            return this;
6255        long mash;
6256        for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
6257            mash = rng.nextLong();
6258            for (int j = i; j < preservation; j++) {
6259                mash |= rng.nextLong();
6260            }
6261            data[i] &= mash;
6262        }
6263        tallied = false;
6264        return this;
6265    }
6266
6267    /**
6268     * Randomly removes points from a GreasedRegion, with preservation as a fraction between 1.0 (keep all) and 0.0
6269     * (remove all). If preservation is 0.5, roughly 1/2 of all points will be removed; if 0.25, roughly 3/4 will be
6270     * removed (roughly 0.25 will be _kept_), if 0.8, roughly 1/5 will be removed (and about 0.8 will be kept), and so
6271     * on. Preservation must be between 0.0 and 1.0 for this to have the intended behavior; 1.0 or higher will keep all
6272     * points without change (returning this GreasedRegion), while anything less than 0.015625 (1.0/64) will empty this
6273     * GreasedRegion (using {@link #empty()}) and then return it. The parameter {@code random} can be an object like a
6274     * {@link DiverRNG}, an {@link RNG} backed by a well-distributed RandomnessSource like its default, DiverRNG, a
6275     * {@link GWTRNG} (especially if you target GWT, where it will perform much better than most alternatives), or any
6276     * of various other RandomnessSource implementations that distribute bits well for
6277     * {@link RandomnessSource#nextLong()}, but should not be intentionally-biased RNGs like {@link DharmaRNG} or 
6278     * {@link EditRNG}, nor double-based QRNGs like {@link VanDerCorputQRNG} or {@link SobolQRNG}.
6279     * @param random used to determine random factors; likely to be an {@link RNG}, {@link DiverRNG}, or {@link GWTRNG}
6280     * @param preservation the rough fraction of points to keep, between 0.0 and 1.0
6281     * @return a randomly modified change to this GreasedRegion
6282     */
6283    public GreasedRegion deteriorate(final RandomnessSource random, final double preservation) {
6284        if(random == null || width <= 2 || ySections <= 0 || preservation >= 1)
6285            return this;
6286        if(preservation <= 0)
6287            return empty();
6288        int bitCount = (int) (preservation * 64);
6289        for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
6290            data[i] &= approximateBits(random, bitCount);
6291        }
6292        tallied = false;
6293        return this;
6294    }
6295
6296    /**
6297     * Inverts the on/off state of the cell with the given x and y.
6298     * @param x the x position of the cell to flip
6299     * @param y the y position of the cell to flip
6300     * @return this for chaining, modified
6301     */
6302    public GreasedRegion flip(int x, int y) {
6303        if(x >= 0 && y >= 0 && x < width && y < height && ySections > 0)
6304        {
6305            data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] ^= (1L << (y & 63));
6306            tallied = false;
6307        }
6308        return this;
6309
6310    }
6311
6312    /**
6313     * Returns a new GreasedRegion that has been mirrored along the rightmost edge, parallel to the y-axis. The new
6314     * GreasedRegion will have exactly twice the width, the additional width will have the contents of the original
6315     * GreasesRegion in reversed order. The positions shared by both GreasedRegions will be the same, that is, any area
6316     * not added to the original will be equal to the original.
6317     * @return a new GreasedRegion with twice the width of {@code this}, that is mirrored along the rightmost edge
6318     */
6319    public GreasedRegion mirrorY()
6320    {
6321        GreasedRegion next = new GreasedRegion(data, width, height, width * 2, height);
6322        for (int i = 0, o = width * 2 - 1; i < width; i++, o--) {
6323            System.arraycopy(data, ySections * i, next.data, ySections * o, ySections);
6324        }
6325        return next;
6326    }
6327
6328    @Override
6329    public boolean intersectsWith(Zone other) {
6330        if (other instanceof GreasedRegion)
6331            return intersects((GreasedRegion) other);
6332        long t, w;
6333        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6334            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
6335                if ((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0) {
6336                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6337                    while (w != 0) {
6338                        if (other.contains(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)))
6339                            return true;
6340                        t ^= w;
6341                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6342                    }
6343                }
6344            }
6345        }
6346        return false;
6347    }

6352     */
6353    @Override
6354    public GreasedRegion translate(Coord c) {
6355        return copy().translate(c.x, c.y);

6372     * Gets a new Zone that contains all the Coords in {@code this} plus all
6373     * neighboring Coords, which can be orthogonally or diagonally adjacent
6374     * to any Coord this has in it. Related to the expand() methods in
6375     * CoordPacker and GreasedRegion, but guaranteed to use 8-way adjacency
6376     * and to return a new Zone. This implementation returns a GreasedRegion

6378     * @return A new GreasedRegion where "off" cells adjacent to {@code this}
6379     *         (orthogonally or diagonally) have been added to the "on" cells
6380     *         in {@code this}

6387    /**
6388     * Checks if {@code c} is present in this GreasedRegion. Returns true if and only if c is present in this
6389     * GreasedRegion as an "on" cell. This will never be true if c is null, has negative x or y, has a value for x that
6390     * is equal to or greater than {@link #width}, or has a value for y that is equal to or greater than
6391     * {@link #height}, but none of those conditions will cause Exceptions to be thrown.
6392     * @param c a Coord to try to find in this GreasedRegion; if null this will always return false
6393     * @return true if {@code c} is an "on" cell in this GreasedRegion, or false otherwise, including if c is null
6394     */
6395    @Override
6396    public boolean contains(Coord c) {
6397        return c != null && contains(c.x, c.y);
6398    }

6400    /**
6401     * Checks whether all Coords in {@code other} are also present in {@code this}.
6402     * Requires that {@code other} won't give a null Coord while this method iterates over it.
6403     * @param other another Zone, such as a GreasedRegion or a {@link squidpony.squidgrid.zone.CoordPackerZone}
6404     * @return true if all Coords in other are "on" in this GreasedRegion, or false otherwise
6405     */
6406    @Override
6407    public boolean contains(Zone other) {
6408        if(other instanceof Collection)
6409            return containsAll((Collection) other);
6410        for(Coord c : other)
6411        {
6412            if(!contains(c.x, c.y))
6413                return false;
6414        }
6415        return true;
6416    }
6417
6418    /**
6419     * @param smallestOrBiggest if true, finds the smallest x-coordinate value;
6420     *                          if false, finds the biggest.
6421     * @return The x-coordinate of the Coord within {@code this} that has the
6422     * smallest (or biggest) x-coordinate. Or -1 if the zone is empty.
6423     */
6424    @Override
6425    public int x(boolean smallestOrBiggest) {
6426        if(smallestOrBiggest)
6427            return first().x;
6428        else
6429            return nth(size()-1).x;
6430    }
6431
6432    /**
6433     * @param smallestOrBiggest if true, finds the smallest y-coordinate value;
6434     *                          if false, finds the biggest.
6435     * @return The y-coordinate of the Coord within {@code this} that has the
6436     * smallest (or biggest) y-coordinate. Or -1 if the zone is empty.
6437     */
6438    @Override
6439    public int y(boolean smallestOrBiggest) {
6440        long t, w;
6441        if(smallestOrBiggest) {
6442            int best = Integer.MAX_VALUE;
6443            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6444                for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
6445                    if ((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0) {
6446                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6447                        while (w != 0) {
6448                            best = Math.min(s << 6 | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w), best);
6449                            if(best == 0)
6450                                return 0;
6451                            t ^= w;
6452                            w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6453                        }
6454                    }
6455                }
6456            }
6457            return best == Integer.MAX_VALUE ? -1 : best;
6458        }
6459        else
6460        {
6461            int best = -1;
6462            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6463                for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
6464                    if ((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0) {
6465                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6466                        while (w != 0) {
6467                            best = Math.max(s << 6 | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w), best);
6468                            if(best == height - 1)
6469                                return best;
6470                            t ^= w;
6471                            w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6472                        }
6473                    }
6474                }
6475            }
6476            return best;
6477        }
6478    }
6479
6480    /**
6481     * Gets the distance between the minimum x-value contained in this GreasedRegion and the maximum x-value in it.
6482     * Not the same as accessing the field {@link #width} on a GreasedRegion! The field will get the span of the space
6483     * that the GreasedRegion can use, including "on" and "off" cells. This method will only get the distance between
6484     * the furthest-separated "on" cells on the x-axis, and won't consider "off" cells. This method can return -1 if the
6485     * GreasedRegion is empty, 0 if the "on" cells are all in a vertical line (that is, when the minimum x is equal to
6486     * the maximum x), or a positive int in other cases with multiple x-values.
6487     * @return the distance on the x-axis between the "on" cell with the lowest x-value and the one with the highest
6488     */
6489    @Override
6490    public int getWidth() {
6491        if (super.width == -2)
6492            super.width = isEmpty() ? -1 : x(false) - x(true);
6493        return super.width;
6494    }
6495    /**
6496     * Gets the distance between the minimum y-value contained in this GreasedRegion and the maximum y-value in it.
6497     * Not the same as accessing the field {@link #height} on a GreasedRegion! The field will get the span of the space
6498     * that the GreasedRegion can use, including "on" and "off" cells. This method will only get the distance between
6499     * the furthest-separated "on" cells on the y-axis, and won't consider "off" cells. This method can return -1 if the
6500     * GreasedRegion is empty, 0 if the "on" cells are all in a horizontal line (that is, when the minimum y is equal to
6501     * the maximum y), or a positive int in other cases with multiple y-values.
6502     * @return the distance on the y-axis between the "on" cell with the lowest y-value and the one with the highest
6503     */
6504    @Override
6505    public int getHeight() {
6506        if (super.height == -2)
6507            super.height = isEmpty() ? -1 : y(false) - y(true);
6508        return super.height;
6509    }
6510
6511    /**
6512     * Gets the diagonal distance from the point combining the lowest x-value present in this GreasedRegion with the
6513     * lowest y-value in this, to the point combining the highest x-value and the highest y-value. These minimum and
6514     * maximum values don't necessarily match a single "on" cell for each min and max corner, and can take their x and y
6515     * values from two different points. The diagonal distance uses Euclidean measurement (basic Pythagorean Theorem
6516     * math here), and will be a double.
6517     * @return the diagonal distance from (min x, min y) to (max x, max y), as a double
6518     */
6519    @Override
6520    public double getDiagonal() {
6521        final int w = getWidth();
6522        final int h = getHeight();
6523        return Math.sqrt((w * w) + (h * h));
6524    }

6529//    }

6531    @Override
6532    public GreasedRegion getInternalBorder() {
6533        return copy().surface8way();
6534    }
6535
6536    /**
6537     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a deterministic but random-seeming
6538     * scattering of chosen cells with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells
6539     * in this. This is pseudo-random with the given seed (which will be made into an odd number if it is not one
6540     * already), and is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as {@link #separatedZCurve(double, int)}, and
6541     * much faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, but
6542     * a fraction value of 0.4 reliably has had no overlap in testing. Restricts the total size of the returned array to
6543     * a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells are "on"). If limit is negative, this will not restrict the
6544     * size.
6545     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
6546     * @param limit the maximum size of the array to return
6547     * @param seed a long seed to change the points; the most significant 21 bits (except the sign bit) and least significant bit are ignored
6548     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the pseudo-random cells
6549     */
6550    public Coord[] mixedRandomSeparatedAlt(double fraction, int limit, long seed)
6551    {
6552        if(fraction < 0)
6553            return new Coord[0];
6554        if(fraction > 1)
6555            fraction = 1;
6556        int tmp, ic;
6557        long t, w;
6558        seed |= 1L;
6559        final int total = size();
6560        int ct = (int)(total * fraction);
6561        if(limit >= 0 && limit < ct)
6562            ct = limit;
6563        Coord[] vl = new Coord[ct];
6564        EACH_QUASI:
6565        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++)
6566        {
6567            tmp = (int)(VanDerCorputQRNG.altDetermine(seed, i+1) * total);
6568
6569            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
6570                for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6571                    if ((ic = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
6572                        t = data[x * ySections + s];
6573                        for (--ic; t != 0; ic--) {
6574                            w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6575                            if (ic == tmp)
6576                            {
6577                                vl[i] = Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.bitCount(w-1));
6578                                continue EACH_QUASI;
6579                            }
6580                            t ^= w;
6581                        }
6582                    }
6583                }
6584            }
6585        }
6586        return vl;
6587    }
6588
6589
6590    public class GRIterator implements Iterator<Coord>
6591    {
6592        public int index = 0;
6593        private long t, w;
6594        public GRIterator()
6595        {
6596            if(!tallied)
6597                tally();
6598        }
6599        @Override
6600        public boolean hasNext() {
6601            return index < ct;
6602        }
6603
6604        @Override
6605        public Coord next() {
6606            int c;
6607            if(index >= ct)
6608                return null;
6609            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
6610                for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6611                    if ((c = counts[x * ySections + s]) > index) {
6612                        t = data[x * ySections + s] | 0L;
6613                        for (--c; t != 0; c--) {
6614                            w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6615                            if (c == index)
6616                            {
6617                                index++;
6618                                return Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.bitCount(w-1));
6619                            }
6620                            t ^= w;
6621                        }
6622                    }
6623                }
6624            }
6625            return null;
6626
6627            /*
6628            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6629                for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
6630                    if ((w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(data[x * ySections + s])) != 0 && i++ >= index) {
6631                        if(index++ < limit)
6632                            return Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
6633                        else
6634                            return null;
6635                    }
6636                }
6637            }
6638            */
6639        }
6640
6641        @Override
6642        public void remove() {
6643            throw new UnsupportedOperationException("remove() is not supported on this Iterator.");
6644        }
6645    }
